The show was broadcast Friday nights at 8:30/7:30c on ABC.<ref name=ABCpilot2>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1670541/reba-mcentire-planning-pilot-for-abc-sitcom-malibu-country.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120320115027/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1670541/reba-mcentire-planning-pilot-for-abc-sitcom-malibu-country.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=March 20, 2012|title=Reba McEntire Planning Pilot for ABC Sitcom, Malibu Country |publisher=[[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]]|date=September 9, 2011}}</ref> On May 11, 2012, McEntire tweeted that the show had been picked up.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/reba-mcentire-malibu-country-series-picked-up-abc|title=Reba McEntire Series 'Malibu Country' Picked Up by ABC|publisher=Taste of Country |date=May 12, 2012 |access-date=December 16, 2012}}</ref> She also was the host in the 2011 NASCAR Award Show in Las Vegas.\n\nDespite reports that ''Malibu Country'' was the most-watched freshman comedy in its debut season (8.7 million),<ref>{{cite web|url=http://tvbythenumbers.zap2it.com/2012/11/28/last-man-standing-and-malibu-country-get-5-more-episodes/159564/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121202060832/http://tvbythenumbers.zap2it.com/2012/11/28/last-man-standing-and-malibu-country-get-5-more-episodes/159564/|url-status=dead|archive-date=December 2, 2012|title='Last Man Standing' and 'Malibu Country' Get 5 More Episodes Each|last=Seidman|first=Robert |publisher=[[TV by the Numbers]] |date=November 28, 2012|access-date=November 29, 2012}}</ref> the show was canceled on May 10, 2013, after eighteen episodes.\n\nIn 2016, McEntire was a guest panelist during [[America's Got Talent (season 11)|season 11]] of ''[[America's Got Talent]]''. During one of the Judge Cuts, McEntire gave the Golden Buzzer to contortionist [[Sofie Dossi]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.ibtimes.com.au/americas-got-talent-2016-update-self-taught-contortionist-sofie-dossi-earns-golden-buzzer-1522089|title='America's Got Talent 2016' update: Self-taught contortionist Sofie Dossi earns golden buzzer|last=Bayos|first=Kris|date=July 18, 2016|work=[[International Business Times]]|access-date=February 21, 2023}}</ref>\n\nIn January 2017, it was announced that McEntire would star and produce a Southern drama series for ABC titled ''Red Blooded''.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2017/01/abc-marc-cherry-southern-drama-pilot-reba-mcentire-stars-1201882258/|title=Marc Cherry Southern Drama Starring Reba McEntire Gets ABC Pilot Order|first=Nellie|last=Andreeva|date=January 10, 2017 |access-date=January 10, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://variety.com/2017/tv/news/reba-mcentire-marc-cherry-abc-drama-pilot-1201956667/|title=Reba McEntire and Marc Cherry Series Picked Up to Pilot at ABC|first=Elizabeth|last=Wagmeister|date=January 10, 2017|website=Variety|access-date=January 10, 2017}}</ref> It was reported in May that ABC ultimately turned down the show, so it moved to being shopped around to other networks.<ref>{{cite web|title=It's Your Call: Cable Considers Reba's \"Red-Blooded,\" after ABC reportedly passes|url=http://abcnewsradioonline.com/music-news/2017/5/16/its-your-call-cable-considers-rebas-red-blooded-after-abc-re.html|website=ABC News Radio|language=en|access-date=October 18, 2017|archive-date=October 19, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171019061546/http://abcnewsradioonline.com/music-news/2017/5/16/its-your-call-cable-considers-rebas-red-blooded-after-abc-re.html|url-status=dead}}</ref> In January 2018, Reba was chosen to portray [[KFC]]'s first female [[Colonel Sanders]]. The commercials ran through the end of April 2018.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/reba-mcentire-as-colonel-sanders-kfc-2018-01-26/|title=Reba McEntire to play KFC's Colonel Sanders|date=January 26, 2018|website=CBS News}}</ref>\n\nIn 2020, McEntire launched a podcast titled ''Living & Learning'' hosted by herself and her former ''[[Reba (TV series)|Reba]]'' co-star [[Melissa Peterman]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://people.com/country/reba-mcentire-debuts-living-learning-spotify-podcast/|title=Reba McEntire Reunites with Melissa Peterman on New Podcast: 'We Make a Good Team!'|website=People.com}}</ref>\n\nShe made a cameo appearance in the 2021 comedy film ''[[Barb and Star Go to Vista Del Mar]]'' as a water spirit named ''Trish'' after [[Annie Mumolo]] and [[Kristen Wiig]], who wrote, produced, and starred in the film, wrote her an \"impassioned letter\" asking her to join the film. Director [[Josh Greenbaum]] said in an interview, \"There's some casting that just clicks. Reba is not only 100% authentic, we knew she would be game.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/entertainment/movies/2021/02/16/barb-star-go-vista-del-mar-reba-mcentire-reveals-cameo/6757814002/|title=Surprise! Reba McEntire reveals her crazy cameo in 'Barb & Star Go to Vista Del Mar'|date=February 16, 2021|website=USA Today}}</ref>\n\nIn May 2022, ABC announced that McEntire will be joining the cast of the drama ''[[Big Sky (American TV series)|Big Sky]]'', playing local businesswoman Sunny Barnes in season 3.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://deadline.com/2022/05/big-sky-reba-mcentire-season-3-abc-drama-series-regular-1235023823/|title='Big Sky': Reba McEntire Joins Season 3 Of ABC Drama As Series Regular|website=Deadline Hollywood|first=Denise|last=Petski|date=May 16, 2022|access-date=May 16, 2022}}</ref>\n\nMcEntire starred in ''[[Reba McEntire's The Hammer]]'' on Lifetime in 2023. The country star will reunite with her ''Reba'' sitcom co-star Melissa Peterman in the film inspired by the life of traveling Nevada circuit judge Kim Wheeler.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Iahn |first=Buddy |date=2022-06-30 |title=Lifetime announces Reba-starring 'The Hammer' |url=https://themusicuniverse.com/lifetime-announces-reba-starring-hammer/ |access-date=2022-08-20 |website=The Music Universe |language=en-US}}</ref> The film also stars McEntire's boyfriend Rex Linn as Bart Crawford, a mysterious cowboy with unknown motives, and Kay Shioma Metchie as Vicky, the tough talking bailiff who serves as Kim's right hand and trusted friend.\n\nIn May 2023, it was announced that McEntire would be a coach on ''[[The Voice (American TV series)|The Voice]]'', replacing [[Blake Shelton]]. She has served as a coach since its [[The Voice (American TV series) season 24|24th season]].<ref>{{Cite web |date=2023-05-15 |title=Reba McEntire to fill Blake Shelton's cowboy boots as coach on \"The Voice\" |url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/reba-mcentire-to-fill-blake-sheltons-cowboy-boots-as-coach-on-the-voice/ |access-date=2023-05-18 |website=www.cbsnews.com |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn September 20, 2023, McEntire reunited with Sofie Dossi where they collaborated during a result show on [[America's Got Talent (season 18)|season 18]] of ''America's Got Talent'' where McEntire sang \"Can't Even Get the Blues\" while Dossi did her contortion, hand-balancing, and aerial performances.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Reba McEntire Does Duet with Contortionist on \"America's Got Talent\"|url=https://www.today.com/popculture/tv/reba-mcentire-duet-contortionist-sofie-dossi-americas-got-talent-rcna116843|first=Drew|last=Weisholtz|publisher=Today|date=September 22, 2023|access-date=September 22, 2023}}</ref>\n\nIn January 2024, it was announced that McEntire was creating a new comedy for NBC, later announced to be titled ''[[Happy's Place (2024 show)|Happy's Place]]'' and co-starring Melissa Peterman who also co-starred in ''[[Reba (TV series)|Reba]]'' with McEntire.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Cordero |first=Rosy |date=2024-01-30 |title=Reba McEntire Reunites With 'Reba' Team On New NBC Comedy Pilot |url=https://deadline.com/2024/01/reba-mcentire-nbc-comedy-pilot-1235808110/ |access-date=2024-01-30 |website=Deadline |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn May 21, 2024, [[Asher HaVon]], a member of Reba's team, won ''The Voice'', making Reba the winning coach on her second season.{{cn|date=August 2024}}\n\n==Musical styles and legacy==\nMcEntire's sound has been influenced by the country music of [[Bob Wills]], [[Merle Haggard]], [[Dolly Parton]], [[Barbara Mandrell]], and [[Patsy Cline]].<ref name=\"book\">{{cite book|last=Nash|first=Alanna|title=''Will the Circle Be Unbroken: Country Music in America'' |publisher=DK Publishing, Inc|location=New York, USA|page=316|chapter=Ch. 11&nbsp;\u2013 Tell Me 'Bout the Good Old Days|date=2006 |isbn=0-7566-2353-7}}</ref> In college, McEntire attended local dances at the Oklahoma\u2013Texas border so she could dance to Wills's music, commenting that, \"it didn't get any better than dancing to Bob Wills music\". She also explained Merle Haggard's influence on her career, stating \"I had every album he ever put out\", and would sing \"every song he did\", along with her brother, Pake and sister, Susie. In addition, her first major hit, \"[[Sweet Dreams (Don Gibson song)|Sweet Dreams]]\" was a remake of Patsy Cline's version of the song, according to McEntire herself.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kovideo.net/lyrics/r/Reba-Mcentire/San-Antonio-Rose.html|archive-url=https://archive.today/20120804050603/http://www.kovideo.net/lyrics/r/Reba-Mcentire/San-Antonio-Rose.html|url-status=dead|archive-date=August 4, 2012|title=\"San Antionio Rose\" lyrics (including citing McEntire's musical influences, beneath lyrics)|publisher=Kovideo.net|access-date=August 27, 2009}}</ref>\n\nMcEntire's music has been described not only to be built upon traditional country music, but also expand into the genres of [[country pop]], [[Pop music|mainstream pop]], [[Soul music|soul]], and [[Rhythm and Blues|R&B]]. At times, her music has been criticized for moving away from traditional country music. Many music critics have called her music to be \"melodramatic\", \"formulaic\", and \"bombastic\", particularly after her 1988 album ''[[Reba (album)|Reba]].'' Studio releases such as ''[[Sweet Sixteen (Reba McEntire album)|Sweet Sixteen]]'', ''[[Rumor Has It (Reba McEntire album)|Rumor Has It]]'', ''[[It's Your Call]]'', and ''[[Starting Over (Reba McEntire album)|Starting Over]]'' have been described by these terms.<ref name=\"roughguide\" />\n\nMcEntire possesses a [[contralto]] vocal range<ref name=\"blog\">{{cite web|url=http://blogs.orlandosentinel.com/entertainment_music_blog/2007/09/larger-than-lif.html|title=Larger than life Reba breaks in UCF Arena, both get high marks|last=Brunson|first=Rick|date=September 9, 2007|publisher=[[Orlando Sentinel]]|access-date=August 27, 2009|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090403222605/http://blogs.orlandosentinel.com/entertainment_music_blog/2007/09/larger-than-lif.html|archive-date=April 3, 2009}}</ref> and performs \"vocal gymnastics\" with her voice,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://mykindofcountry.wordpress.com/2009/08/12/album-review-reba-mcentire-reba/|title=Album review: ''Reba'' (1988)|last=Morrow|first=Megan |date=August 12, 2009|publisher=My Kind of Country|access-date=August 27, 2009}}</ref> a musical technique in which a singer twirls a note around, using their [[vibrato]]. McEntire has credited Dolly Parton for influencing this trait, stating that she always listened to Parton's records and find her style of vocal gymnastics \"so pretty\".<ref name=\"cmtvideo\">Interview with Reba McEntire for ''CMT Inside Fame'' on Country Music Television; retrieved August 26, 2009.</ref>\n\nMcEntire has often been regarded as one of country music's most influential female vocalists and most beloved entertainers.<ref name=\"roughguide\"/><ref name=\"book\"/> She is highly credited for remaining one of country's most popular female artists for nearly four decades, maintaining her success by continually incorporating contemporary musical sounds without changing her traditional vocal style.<ref name=\"countryuniverse\"/><ref name=\"book\"/> For numerous artists, she has been credited as an inspiration to their careers in music.<ref name=\"book\"/> ''The Net Music Countdown'' second-handedly reported, \"That influence has manifested itself in many ways. As a role model, she's shown others how to handle fame with grace and good humor while never backing down from her values or goals. Just as importantly, she's shown others to refuse to accept limitations on what she can do or how much she can achieve.\" McEntire also explained to the online website, \"Whatever I'm doing, I feel like I'm representing country music\". \"It's always been my main career, and it's where my loyalties lie. I feel like I'm waving the flag of country music wherever I go, and I couldn't be prouder to do it.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.netmusiccountdown.com/inc/artist.php?artist=Reba+McEntire|title=Reba McEntire (originally sourced from her official website)|publisher=The Net Music Countdown|access-date=August 27, 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090716060007/http://www.netmusiccountdown.com/inc/artist.php?artist=Reba+McEntire|archive-date=July 16, 2009|url-status=dead|df=mdy-all}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nMcEntire is a Christian, and she has stated that her faith in God has helped her immensely throughout her life.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.christianpost.com/news/reba-mcentire-relies-on-the-holy-spirit-every-day-reveals-faith-carried-her-through-heartbreak.html|title=Reba McEntire 'relies on the Holy Spirit every day,' reveals faith carried her through heartbreak|work=The Christian Post|first=Leah MarieAnn|last=Klett|date=27 December 2019}}</ref>\n\nTwo of her siblings have also had careers in the music industry. Her brother Pake dabbled in the country music industry in the late 1980s but returned to Oklahoma after a brief stint. He owns and operates a {{convert|1,000|acre|adj=on}} ranch near Coalgate, Oklahoma, and continues to rodeo. Her sister [[Susie McEntire|Susie McEntire-Eaton]] (Martha Susan \"Susie\" McEntire-Eaton, formerly Luchsinger) is a successful Christian music singer who travels the country with her husband, speaking and performing. She also has an older sister, Alice Foran, a retired social worker who resides in Lane, Oklahoma. Her niece Calamity McEntire is the Associate Head Coach for the [[University of Illinois]] women's basketball team.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.mylifetime.com/lifestyle/entertainment/celebrities/many-sides-reba-mcentire|title=The Many Sides of Reba McEntire|last=Hay|first=Carla|publisher=Lifetime.com|access-date=September 1, 2009|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100225145438/http://www.mylifetime.com/lifestyle/entertainment/celebrities/many-sides-reba-mcentire|archive-date=February 25, 2010}}</ref><ref> Calamity McEntire: Associate Head Coach. Fighting Illini Staff Directory. https://fightingillini.com/staff-directory/calamity-mcentire/1911 </ref>\n=== Relationships and family ===\nIn 1976, McEntire married [[steer wrestling]] champion and rancher Charlie Battles, who was 10 years her senior and had two sons from his previous marriage. The couple shared a ranch in Oklahoma. In 1987, McEntire divorced Battles and moved to Nashville, Tennessee, to further pursue her career.<ref>{{cite web|title=Reba McEntire Profile|url=http://www.cnn.com/CNN/Programs/people/shows/mcentire/profile.html|website=People in the News|publisher=Cable news Network LP, LLPP|access-date=November 24, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Dignity Memorial|url=http://obits.dignitymemorial.com/dignity-memorial/obituary.aspx?n=Charlie-Battles&lc=2591&pid=164399527&mid=5505776|website=HIXSON-SULPHUR MEMORIAL FUNERAL HOME|publisher=SCI Shared Resources, LLC|access-date=November 24, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Monaco|first1=Rachael|title=5 moments that changed Reba McEntire's life and career|url=https://www.axs.com/5-moments-that-changed-reba-mcentire-s-life-and-career-53250|website=Axs.com|access-date=November 24, 2017}}</ref>\n\nIn 1989, McEntire married her manager and former steel guitar player Narvel Blackstock. The couple wed at Lake Tahoe on a boat in a private ceremony. Together, the pair took over all aspects of McEntire's career, forming Starstruck Entertainment, which was originally designed to help manage her career. From her marriage to Blackstock, McEntire gained three stepchildren, Chassidy, Shawna, and Brandon. She gave birth to a son, [[Shelby Blackstock|Shelby Steven McEntire Blackstock]], in February 1990. On August 3, 2015, it was announced in a joint statement on McEntire's website that she and Blackstock had been separated for a few months after 26 years of marriage.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Saad|first1=Nardine|title=Reba McEntire splits from husband-manager Narvel Blackstock|url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment/gossip/la-et-mg-reba-mcentire-split-narvel-blackstock-separate-20150803-story.html|newspaper=[[Los Angeles Times]]}}</ref> McEntire announced in December 2015 that their divorce had been finalized on October 28, 2015. Despite the divorce, McEntire remains very close to her three stepchildren and the Blackstock family; she considers her stepchildren's children to be her grandchildren.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.people.com/article/reba-mcentire-narvel-blackstock-divorce-finalized-facebook?xid=rss-topheadlines|title=Reba McEntire Confirms Date of Divorce From Ex-Husband Narvel Blackstock on Facebook|work=People|date=December 19, 2015|access-date=December 19, 2015|author=Karen Mizoguchi}}</ref>\n\nMcEntire's stepson Brandon Blackstock married singer [[Kelly Clarkson]], with whom he has a daughter and a son.<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.usmagazine.com/celebrity-news/news/kelly-clarkson-marries-fiance-brandon-blackstock-in-tennessee-all-the-details-20132110/|title=Kelly Clarkson Marries Fiance Brandon Blackstock In Tennessee \u2013 All the Details!|work=Us Weekly|date=October 21, 2013| access-date=December 14, 2022|first=Stephanie|last=Webber}}</ref> Speaking about their impending marriage in 2013, McEntire stated she was \"Thrilled to death, to have my buddy as my daughter-in-law. I mean, who could ask for more?\"<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.eonline.com/news/387882/reba-mcentire-thrilled-to-death-to-have-kelly-clarkson-as-daughter-in-law|title=Reba McEntire \"Thrilled to Death\" to Have Kelly Clarkson as Daughter-in-Law|work=E!|date=February 12, 2013|access-date=December 14, 2022|first=Bruna|last=Nessif}}</ref> Blackstock and Clarkson's divorce was finalized in March 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Kelly Clarkson Settles Divorce, Will Pay Brandon Blackstock Over $1.3M Plus Monthly Spousal Support |url=https://people.com/music/kelly-clarkson-settles-divorce-from-brandon-blackstock/ |access-date=2022-11-26 |website=People.com |language=en}}</ref> [[File:Reba McEntire & Rex Linn (51935656397).jpg |thumb|right|McEntire with her boyfriend [[Rex Linn]] in 2022]] \n\nIn 2017, McEntire began a relationship with photographer Anthony \"Skeeter\" Lasuzzo. The couple met through McEntire's association with [[Kix Brooks]]. In describing her feelings about Lasuzzo, she stated in April 2019, \"We're totally in love \u2014 absolutely,\" she says. \"I wouldn't put up with somebody for two years if I wasn't in love with 'em!\"<ref>{{cite web |last1=Kruh |first1=Nancy |title=Reba McEntire's in Love! And No One Is More Surprised Than She Is: 'I Was Not Looking' |url=https://www.yahoo.com/entertainment/reba-mcentire-apos-love-no-120054031.html |website=[[People (magazine)|People]]|date=April 4, 2019 }}</ref> McEntire and Lasuzzo separated six months later.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usmagazine.com/celebrity-news/news/reba-mcentire-skeeter-lasuzzo-split-after-2-years-together/|title=Reba McEntire Confirms Split From Boyfriend Skeeter Lasuzzo After 2 Years of Dating|last=Jackson|first=Dory|work=[[Us Weekly]]|date=November 5, 2019|access-date=November 6, 2019}}</ref>\n\nIn 2020, McEntire began dating film and TV actor [[Rex Linn]].<ref>{{cite web | url=https://people.com/country/reba-mcentire-rex-linn-relationship-timeline/ | title=Reba McEntire and Rex Linn's Relationship Timeline }}</ref> They first met on the set of ''The Gambler Returns: The Luck of the Draw'' (1991) and reconnected almost thirty years later when McEntire guest-starred as June on ''Young Sheldon'', where Linn has a recurring role as principal of Sheldon's high school.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.vulture.com/2023/10/wwhl-reba-mcentire-young-sheldon.html | title=Reba McEntire Owes Her Relationship to Young Sheldon | date=October 11, 2023 }}</ref>\n\n=== Philanthropy ===\nIn 1992, she opened Reba's Ranch House in Denison, Texas,<ref>{{cite web |title=The House that Reba Built FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE |url=https://www.texomahealth.org/2016celebration/Press_Release/press_release.html |website=Texoma Health |access-date=7 December 2018 |archive-date=December 9, 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181209124611/https://www.texomahealth.org/2016celebration/Press_Release/press_release.html |url-status=dead }}</ref> an extended-stay residence for relatives of patients undergoing treatment at [[Texoma Medical Center]] or other nearby facilities.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.ntxe-news.com/cgi-bin/artman/exec/view.cgi?archive=11&num=27497&printer=1|title=Reba benefit raises over half a million dollars|author=TMC|date=July 29, 2005|work=North Texas e-News}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://blog.scoutingmagazine.org/2023/10/11/country-music-superstar-buys-popcorn-from-local-cub-scouts/|title=Country music superstar buys popcorn from local Cub Scouts|work=Scouting Magazine|date=October 11, 2023|first=Aaron|last=Derr}}</ref>\n\nOver the course of her career, she has been and continues to be an active supporter of various charitable organizations including [[Habitat for Humanity]], [[The Salvation Army]], the [[American Red Cross]], [[Feeding America]] and Celebrity Fight Night. She has been honored with the [[Minnie Pearl]] Award, the ACM Home Depot Humanitarian Award and the [[Andrea Bocelli]] Foundation Humanitarian Award for her efforts. In 2018, she was honored with the [[Horatio Alger]] Award for Education, Charity Work. Named after the \"rags to riches\" writer, the award recognizes perseverance and giving back.<ref>{{cite news |title=Reba McEntire to Receive Horatio Alger Award for Education, Charity Work |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/reba-mcentire-to-receive-horatio-alger-award-for-education-charity-work-200568/ |access-date=7 December 2018 |publisher=Rolling Stone |date=19 December 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Young |first1=McKenna |title=Iconic Entertainer and Grammy Award-Winning Country Superstar Reba McEntire to Receive 2018 Horatio Alger Award |url=https://horatioalger.org/haa_news/iconic-entertainer-and-grammy-award-winning-country-superstar-reba-mcentire-to-receive-2018-horatio-alger-award/ |website=Horatio Alger |access-date=7 December 2018 |archive-date=December 9, 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181209123724/https://horatioalger.org/haa_news/iconic-entertainer-and-grammy-award-winning-country-superstar-reba-mcentire-to-receive-2018-horatio-alger-award/ |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=REBA MCENTIRE PRESENTED WITH ANDREA BOCELLI FOUNDATION HUMANITARIAN AWARD |url=http://theboot.com/reba-mcentire-andrea-bocelli-foundation-humanitarian-award/ |access-date=7 December 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Accolades==\n{{Main|List of awards and nominations received by Reba McEntire}}\nMcEntire has the second-most wins for the [[Academy of Country Music]]'s Top Female Vocalist Awards with seven. McEntire holds the record [[American Music Awards]] for Favorite Country Female Artist (twelve). She also holds the distinction of being the first to win the [[Country Music Association]]'s Female Vocalist of the Year Award four times consecutively. [[Martina McBride]] won Female Vocalist four times, although not consecutively. In 2013, [[Miranda Lambert]] tied McEntire to win Female Vocalist four years in a row and in 2016 [[Carrie Underwood]] joined this elite club by winning her fourth Female Vocalist award. McEntire is also a rare musical artist to achieve solo number-ones across four decades (1980s, 1990s, 2000s, 2010s). She holds the record for 2nd most CMA Award nominations for a female artist, with 51. McEntire also holds the record with the most ACM Awards nominations for a female artist with 47, respectively.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.acmcountry.com/winners|title=Academy of Country Music Awards winners|work=E!|date=September 12, 2017|first=Reba|last=McEntire}}</ref> She is also the recipient of three [[Grammy Awards]], winning in 1987, 1994 and 2018. In December 2018, McEntire received the [[Kennedy Center Honors|Kennedy Center Honor]].<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/cher-hamilton-philip-glass-to-receive-kennedy-center-honors-703455/|title= Cher, 'Hamilton,' Philip Glass to Receive Kennedy Center Honors|publisher=Rolling Stone|access-date=July 26, 2018}}</ref>\n\nWhen Reba McEntire made her [[Grand Ole Opry]] debut on September 17, 1977, she almost did not make it in the door after a guard at the Opry gate missed her name on the night's list of performers.<ref name=\"opry.com\">{{cite web|last=Opry|title=Reba McEntire|url=http://www.opry.com/artist/reba-mcentire|access-date=March 14, 2014|archive-date=March 19, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140319020128/http://www.opry.com/artist/reba-mcentire|url-status=dead}}</ref> Her parents and older sister, Alice, drove 1,400 miles round trip from their Oklahoma home to see what turned out to be Reba's three-minute performance that night. Her act was cut from two songs to just one\u2014\"Invitation to the Blues\"\u2014because of a surprise appearance by Dolly Parton.<ref name=\"opry.com\"/> McEntire was inducted into the Grand Ole Opry on January 17, 1986.<ref name=\"opry.com\"/> \"The Grand Ole Opry is a home,\" she says. \"It's a family. It's like a family reunion, when you come back and get to see everybody.\"<ref>{{cite web|last=Thompson|first=Gayle|title=28 Year Ago: Reba McEntire joins the Grand Ole Opry|website=The Boot|url=http://theboot.com/reba-mcentire-grand-ole-opry/|access-date=March 14, 2014}}</ref>\n\nIn 2011, the Country Music Association announced that McEntire would be inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame]].<ref name=\"halloffame\">{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-country-idUSTRE7205H820110301|title=Reba McEntire among Country Hall of Fame inductees|work=Reuters|date=January 3, 2011|access-date=August 29, 2015}}</ref> McEntire was unable to attend the announcement after her father had slipped into a coma following a stroke.<ref name=\"halloffame\"/> McEntire attended the official induction ceremony alongside the other 2011 inductees [[Jean Shepard]] and [[Bobby Braddock]]. She was inducted by [[Dolly Parton]].\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|Reba McEntire albums discography|Reba McEntire singles discography|l2=singles|Reba McEntire videography|l3=videos}}\n\n===Studio Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Vern_Gosdin","to":"Vern Gosdin"}],"pages":{"2533887":{"pageid":2533887,"ns":0,"title":"Vern Gosdin","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music singer (1934\u20132009)}}\n{{More citations needed|date=April 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Vern Gosdin\n| image               = Vern-Gosdin.png\n| caption             = Gosdin performing on TNN, 1999\n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = Vernon Gosdin\n| birth_date          = {{birth date|1934|08|05}}\n| birth_place         = [[Woodland, Alabama]], U.S.\n| death_date          = {{death date and age|2009|04|28|1934|08|05}}\n|death_place          = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| instrument          = [[Vocals]], [[guitar]]\n| genre               = [[Country music|Country]], [[Gospel music|gospel]], [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]], [[folk rock]]\n| occupation          = [[Singing|Singer]], [[songwriter]]\n| years_active        = 1967\u20132009\n| label               = [[Elektra Records|Elektra]]<br>[[Ovation Records|Ovation]]<br>AMI<br>[[A&M Records|A&M]]<br>Compleat<br>[[Columbia Records]]<br />VGM\n| past_member_of     = [[Emmylou Harris]]<br />[[George Jones]]<br />[[George Strait]]\n}}\n\n'''Vernon Gosdin''' (August 5, 1934<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=163/4}}</ref> \u2013 April 28, 2009)<ref name=\"Obit\"/> aka Country music's \"The Voice\", was an American [[country music]] [[singing|singer]]. He had 19 top-10 solo hits on the country music charts from 1977 through 1990. Three of these hits went to Number One: \"[[I Can Tell By the Way You Dance (You're Gonna Love Me Tonight)]]\", \"[[Set 'Em Up Joe]]\", and \"[[I'm Still Crazy]]\".<ref name=\"jw40\">Whitburn, Joel (1996). ''The Billboard Book of Top 40 Country Hits'', p.129-130. {{ISBN|0-8230-7632-6}}.</ref>\n\n==Career==\n===Early years===\nAs the sixth child in a family of nine,<ref name=\"jw1-575\">Whitburn, Joel (1991). ''The Billboard Book of Number One Country Hits'', p.575. {{ISBN|0-8230-7553-2}}.</ref> Vern Gosdin began singing in Bethel East Baptist Church in his birth place of [[Woodland, Alabama]], United States,<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> where his mother played piano. Gosdin and two brothers sang gospel on [[Birmingham, Alabama|Birmingham]] radio station [[WJOX (AM)|WVOK]].<ref name=\"jw1-575\"/> Gosdin later moved to [[Chicago, Illinois]], where he operated the D&G Tap. He idolized [[The Louvin Brothers]] and [[The Blue Sky Boys]] as a young man.{{citation needed|date=February 2013}}\n\n===1960s: West Coast Country music movement===\nIn 1961, Gosdin moved to California, where he joined the West Coast Country music movement, first as a member of the Golden State Boys,<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> which became [[The Hillmen]], and included [[Chris Hillman]].<ref name=\"jw1-575\"/> Gosdin then formed The Gosdin Brothers with brother Rex. The duo appeared on the charts in the late 1960s with a song titled \"Hangin' On\" on the Bakersfield International label, then with \"Till The End\" on Capitol Records. During the same time period, the Gosdin Brothers were featured on Hillman's former [[Byrds]] mate [[Gene Clark]]'s first solo album, the 1967 well-regarded ''[[Gene Clark with the Gosdin Brothers]]'',<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\" /> singing backing vocals on all of the tracks behind the lead vocals of Clark and lead guitars of Clarence White, Glen Campbell, and Bill Rinehart (later of the Merry-Go-Round).\n\n===1970s: Retirement and comeback===\nGosdin retired from performing during the 1970s and moved to Cartersville, Georgia, where he operated a glass company.<ref name=\"jw1-575\"/> In 1976, he signed with [[Elektra Records]] and his first hit was a remake of \"Hangin' On\", which featured [[Emmylou Harris]] on harmony vocals and peaked at No.&nbsp;16.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> His next single, \"Yesterday's Gone\" written by Wayne Hinsen Bradford who also wrote for Emmylou Harris, which also featured Harris, became his first Top 10 hit in 1977.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Several more hits followed between 1977 and 1979 with the biggest of these hits being a remake of \"Till the End\" and a cover of [[The Association]]'s \"[[Never My Love]]\" which also featured harmony vocals from [[Janie Frickie]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\n===1981\u20131983: \"Today My World Slipped Away\"===\nIn 1981, Gosdin signed with [[Ovation Records]] and scored a Top 10 hit with \"Dream of Me\". After Ovation Records closed their doors later in 1981, Gosdin signed with A.M.I. Records where he scored a Top 10 hit in 1982 with \"Today My World Slipped Away\". (This song later became a number-three hit for [[George Strait]]).\n\nIn January 1982, during a trial that examined the attempted assassination of music producer [[Gary S. Paxton]], Darryl C. Langley claimed under oath that he and his cohort were hired attackers employed by Gosdin, who worked closely with Paxton and was alleged to be disgruntled in their working relationship. Gosdin was never arrested or charged and repeatedly refused to confirm or deny involvement for the remainder of his life.\n\nGosdin signed with Complete Records in the early 1980s, and, in 1984, released ''There Is A Season'', picked by the ''[[Los Angeles Times]]'' as best country album of the year.\nThe early 1980s also found a great combination of talent as Gosdin traveled from coast to coast opening shows for George Jones.\n\n===1983\u20131985: \"If You're Gonna Do Me Wrong (Do It Right)\"' and ''There Is a Season''===\nGosdin made the top 10 consistently in the early 1980s, really hitting his stride when he teamed with Barnes as a songwriting collaborator. The pair specialized in songs of cheating and barroom romance, often delivering an over-the-top emotionalism that got Gosdin compared to [[George Jones]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> In 1983, Gosdin had two top 5 hits \u2014 \"If You're Gonna Do Me Wrong (Do It Right)\" and \"Way Down Deep\" with the former earning him a nomination for the [[Grammy Award for Best Male Country Vocal Performance|Grammy Award for Best Country Vocal Performance, Male.]] The following year, he had his first No.&nbsp;1 single with \"I Can Tell by the Way You Dance (You're Gonna Love Me Tonight)\",<ref name=\"jw40\"/> which had previously been recorded by [[Gary Morris]].<ref name=\"jw1-575\"/> On September 22, 1985, Gosdin appeared at the original Farm Aid concert at the University of Illinois' Memorial Stadium.\n\n===1987\u20131989: \"Chiseled in Stone\"===\nAfter Compleat Records went bankrupt, Gosdin signed with Columbia in 1987. He immediately had success with \"Do You Believe Me Now\", and scored another No.&nbsp;1 hit with a tribute to [[Ernest Tubb]] called \"Set 'Em Up Joe\".<ref name=\"jw40\"/> Gosdin's \"[[Chiseled in Stone]]\", co-written with Barnes, won the Country Music Association's Song of the Year award in 1989 and earned them a nomination for the [[Grammy Award for Best Country Song]].\n\n===1989\u20131990: ''Alone''===\nGosdin's 1989 album, ''Alone'', was a concept album in a traditional country style. It chronicled the dissolution of Gosdin's marriage and included his final number-one hit: \"I'm Still Crazy\".<ref name=\"jw40\"/> From 1989 to 1991, he released a number of songs and three more made the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' top 10: \"Right in the Wrong Direction\", \"That Just About Does It\" and \"Is It Raining at Your House\". \"Raining\" has been covered by [[Brad Paisley]] and [[Lorrie Morgan]], and \"That Just About Does It\" by [[Willie Nelson]].\n\n===Later years===\nGosdin suffered a stroke in 1998, but he continued writing and singing up until his death. In 2009, Gosdin collaborated with Joe Sins of the country music duo The Sins to write and record his final four songs.\n\n==Death==\nGosdin suffered another stroke in early April 2009, and died at a Nashville hospital on the evening of April 28 at the age of 74.<ref name=\"Obit\">{{Cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1610248/singer-songwriter-vern-gosdin-dies-in-nashville-at-age-74/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150510233623/http://www.cmt.com/news/1610248/singer-songwriter-vern-gosdin-dies-in-nashville-at-age-74/|url-status=dead|archive-date=May 10, 2015|title=Singer-Songwriter Vern Gosdin Dies in Nashville at Age 74|first=Calvin|last=Gilbert|website=CMT News|access-date=August 7, 2021}}</ref> His remains were buried at [[Mount Olivet Cemetery (Nashville)|Mount Olivet Cemetery]] in Nashville, Tennessee.\n\n==Discography==\n{{main|Vern Gosdin discography}}\n\n==Awards and nominations==\n=== Grammy Awards ===\n\n{{awards New York: Oxford University Press. pp.&nbsp;206\u20137.\n\n==External links==\n* [https://web.archive.org/web/20040203193709/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/gosdin_vern/artist.jhtml CMT.com: Vern Gosdin]\n* [https://web.archive.org/web/20090915180259/http://www.thetripwire.com/blog/2009/05/05/sounds-of-goodbye-the-voice-vern-gosdin/ Vern Gosdin remembrance in the Tripwire]\n\n{{Vern Gosdin}}\n{{CMA for Song of the Year}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Gosdin, Vern}}\n[[Category:1934 births]]\n[[Category:2009 deaths]]\n[[Category:American country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:American male singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:People from Randolph County, Alabama]]\n[[Category:Elektra Records artists]]\n[[Category:Columbia Records artists]]\n[[Category:A&M Records artists]]\n[[Category:Ovation Records artists]]\n[[Category:20th-century American singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Tennessee]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Alabama]]\n[[Category:20th-century American male singers]]\n[[Category:Burials at Mount Olivet Cemetery (Nashville)]]\n[[Category:Singer-songwriters from Alabama]]\n[[Category:Singer-songwriters from Tennessee]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Richard_Sterban","to":"Richard Sterban"}],"pages":{"9611578":{"pageid":9611578,"ns":0,"title":"Richard Sterban","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American quartet bass singer (born 1943)}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|image   = Richard_2019.jpg\n|caption = Sterban in 2019\n|background = solo_singer\n|birth_name = Richard Anthony Sterban\n|birth_date = {{birth date and age|mf=yes|1943|4|24}}\n|birth_place =[[Camden, New Jersey|Camden]], [[New Jersey]], U.S.\n|genre    = [[Country music|Country]], [[Southern gospel|gospel]]\n|occupation = Bass singer\n|years_active = 1972\u2013present\n| current_member_of =[[The Oak Ridge Boys]]\n|website = [http://www.oakridgeboys.com/ oakridgeboys.com]\n}}\n'''Richard  Anthony Sterban''' (born April 24, 1943) is an American singer. He was born in [[Camden, New Jersey]]. In 1972, he joined the [[country music|country]] and [[gospel music|gospel]] quartet [[The Oak Ridge Boys]], in which he sings [[bass (voice type)|bass]].\n\nSterban was inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum|Country Music Hall of Fame]] in 2015 as a member of the Oak Ridge Boys.\n\n==Personal life==\n\nBorn in [[Camden, New Jersey]], Sterban grew up in [[Collingswood, New Jersey]],<ref>DeLuca, Dan. [http://articles.philly.com/1994-04-28/entertainment/25861569_1_oak-ridge-boys-hall-oates-plaques \"Today's Walk Of Fame Honorees Include 2 Oak Ridge Boys Just A Couple Of Philly-area Country Boys\"], ''[[The Philadelphia Inquirer]]'', April 28, 1994. Accessed March 10, 2011. \"Bonsall grew up in the Harrowgate section of Philadelphia, near the Tioga Street el stop; Sterban was born across the river in Camden and grew up in Collingswood.\"</ref> After graduating from [[Collingswood High School]], Sterban attended Trenton State College (now [[The College of New Jersey]]).<ref>Lloyd, Jack. [http://articles.philly.com/1991-02-22/entertainment/25775974_1_bonsall-country-music-country-boy \"Sturdy Oaks And A Country Boy From Phila.\"], ''[[The Philadelphia Inquirer]]'', February 22, 1991. Accessed November 13, 2013. \"The remaining member of the Oaks, Richard Sterban, is a native of Camden who graduated from Collingswood High School and attended Trenton State College.\"</ref>\n\n==Career==\n\nPrior to joining The Oak Ridge Boys, Sterban toured with [[J. D. Sumner]] and the [[Stamps Quartet]], who were singing backup for [[Elvis Presley]] at that time. Sterban ultimately became best known for his \"oom-pa-pa-oom-pa-pa-moww-moww\" bass solo in the Oak Ridge Boys' 1981 single \"[[Elvira (song)|Elvira]]\" and sang lead vocals on a select few of the group's songs, including a cover of The Righteous Brothers' hit \"[[Dream On (The Righteous Brothers song)|Dream On]]\", which was a top-ten hit.\n\nSterban has recorded [[public service announcement]]s for [[NOAA Weather Radio]]. He served as the voice of ''[[The Roadhouse]]'', the [[classic country]] [[Sirius Satellite Radio]] [[List of Sirius Satellite Radio stations|channel]]. Sterban was a minority owner of the [[Nashville Sounds]] [[minor league baseball]] team from 1978 to 2008, along with entrepreneur [[Larry Schmittou]] and other country music stars, such as [[Conway Twitty]], [[Larry Gatlin]], and [[Cal Smith]].<ref>{{citation|first=Larry|last=Woody|title=Schmittou: A Grand Slam in Baseball, Business, and Life|publisher=Eggmann Publishing Company|location=Nashville|year=1996|ISBN=1886371334 |pages=64\u201365}}</ref>\n\nSince 2023, Sterban has taken prolonged absences from The Oak Ridge Boys' tours. Aaron McCune, the bass vocalist for [[Dailey & Vincent]], serves as Sterban's designated fill-in.<ref>[https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/aaron-mccune-keeps-bass-singing-alive-with-oak-ridge-boys-dailey-vincent/ Aaron McCune Keeps Bass Singing Alive with Oak Ridge Boys, Dailey & Vincent]. ''Saving Country Music''. February 3, 2023. Retrieved September 20, 2023.</ref> As of September 2023, the band has stated that the issues that led to Sterban's absences have been resolved.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Watts |first=Cindy |date=September 19, 2023 |title=The Oak Ridge Boys Announce Farewell Tour |url=https://www.cmt.com/news/hkt8uf/the-oak-ridge-boys-announce-farewell-tour |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230928110644/https://www.cmt.com/news/hkt8uf/the-oak-ridge-boys-announce-farewell-tour |url-status=dead |archive-date=September 28, 2023 |access-date=2023-09-21 |website=[[Country Music Television|CMT]] |language=en}}</ref>\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n{{The Oak Ridge Boys}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Sterban, Richard}}\n[[Category:1943 births]]\n[[Category:American basses]]\n[[Category:American country singer-songwriters]]\n[[Category:Collingswood High School alumni]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:Musicians from Camden, New Jersey]]\n[[Category:People from Collingswood, New Jersey]]\n[[Category:Singer-songwriters from New Jersey]]\n[[Category:The College of New Jersey alumni]]\n[[Category:The Oak Ridge Boys members]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from New Jersey]]\n[[Category:American male singer-songwriters]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Eddy_Arnold","to":"Eddy Arnold"}],"pages":{"1044945":{"pageid":1044945,"ns":0,"title":"Eddy Arnold","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music singer (1918\u20132008)}}\n{{Other people|Eddy Arnold|Edward Arnold (disambiguation)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=June 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = Eddy Arnold\n| image            = File:Eddie Arnold 1969.JPG\n| caption          = Arnold in 1969\n| image_size       = \n| background       = solo_singer\n| birth_name       = Richard Edward Arnold\n| alias            = The Tennessee Plowboy\n| birth_date       = {{birth date|mf=yes|1918|5|15}}\n| birth_place      = [[Henderson, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| death_date       = {{death date and age|mf=yes|2008|5|8|1918|5|15}}\n| death_place      = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| instrument       = [[Acoustic guitar|Guitar]], [[banjo]]\n| genre            = [[country music|Country]], [[gospel music|gospel]], [[pop music|pop]]\n| occupation       = Singer, songwriter, tv host, actor\n| years_active     = 1934\u20132005\n| label            = [[RCA Victor]] (1944\u20131972; 1976\u20132008)<br />[[MGM Records]] (1973\u20131976)|\n| associated_acts  = [[Ernest Tubb]], [[Hank Snow]], [[Tennessee Ernie Ford]], [[Patsy Cline]], [[Stephen H. Sholes]], [[LeAnn Rimes]]\n| website          = <!--www.eddyarnold.com This is NOT Arnold's \"official\" website -->\n| current_members  = \n| past_members     = \n}}\n\n'''Richard Edward Arnold''' (May 15, 1918 \u2013 May 8, 2008) was an American [[country music]] singer. He was a [[Nashville sound]] (country/popular music) innovator of the late 1950s, and scored 147 songs on the ''[[Billboard Magazine|Billboard]]'' country music charts, second only to [[George Jones]]. He sold more than 85 million records. A member of the [[Grand Ole Opry]] (beginning 1943) and the [[Country Music Hall of Fame]] (beginning 1966), Arnold ranked 22nd on [[Country Music Television]]'s 2003 list of \"The 40 Greatest Men of Country Music.\"\n\n== Early years ==\nArnold was born on May 15, 1918, on a farm near [[Henderson, Tennessee]]. His father, a [[Sharecropping|sharecropper]], played the [[fiddle]], while his mother played guitar. Arnold's father died when he was just 11, forcing him to leave school and begin helping on the family farm. This led to him later gaining his nickname, the '''Tennessee Plowboy'''. Arnold attended [[Pinson High School]] in [[Pinson, Tennessee]], where he played guitar for school functions and events. He quit before graduation to help with the farm work, but continued performing, often arriving on a mule with his guitar hung on his back. Arnold also worked part-time as an assistant at a [[mortuary]].<ref name=\"cmenc\">{{cite book|last=Stambler|first=Irwin|author2=Grelun Landon |author3=Lyndon Stambler |title=Country Music: An Encyclopedia|publisher=Macmillan Publishers|year=2000|pages=17\u201319|isbn=978-0-312-26487-1|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=RjfB6-nVHZIC&q=Eddy+Arnold&pg=PA17|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref>\n[[File:Downtown henderson tennessee.jpg|left|thumb|Downtown Henderson, Tennessee, the city near which Arnold was born]]\n\nIn 1934, at age 16, Arnold made his debut on WTJS-AM in [[Jackson, Tennessee]]. He began performing at local nightclubs and was hired permanently by WTJS in 1937. In 1938, he was hired by WMPS-AM in [[Memphis, Tennessee]], where he was one of its most popular performers. He soon left WMPS for KWK-AM in [[St. Louis, Missouri]],<ref name=\"Streissguth1997\">{{Cite book|first=Michael|last=Streissguth|title=Eddy Arnold: Pioneer of the Nashville Sound|publisher=Schirmer Books|location=New York|year=1997|isbn=0-02-864719-X|url-access=registration|url=https://archive.org/details/eddyarnoldpionee0000stre}}</ref> followed briefly by a spot at WHAS-AM in [[Louisville, Kentucky]].\n\nHe performed for [[WSM (AM)]] on the [[Grand Ole Opry]] during 1943 as a solo artist.<ref name=\"cmenc\" /> In 1944, Arnold signed a contract with [[RCA Victor]], and with manager [[Colonel Tom Parker]] who would later manage [[Elvis Presley]]. Arnold's first single was little noticed,<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.ask.com/music/artist/Eddy-Arnold/1507 |title=What's Your Question? |publisher=Ask.com |access-date=May 1, 2012 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100110013108/http://www.ask.com/music/artist/Eddy-Arnold/1507 |archive-date=January 10, 2010 }}</ref> but the next, \"[[Each Minute Seems a Million Years]]\", scored number five on the country charts in 1945.<ref name=\"cmenc\" /> Its success began a decade of unprecedented chart performance; Arnold's next 57 singles all ranked in the top 10 in the US country charts, including 19 number-one successes.<ref>\"Heartaches By the Number\", Cantwell, David & Friskics-Warren, Bill, 2003, Vanderbilt University Press, pg. 146</ref>\n\nIn 1946, Arnold scored his first major success with \"[[That's How Much I Love You (Eddy Arnold song)|That's How Much I Love You]]\". In 1948, he had five successful songs on the charts simultaneously. That year, he had nine songs in the top 10; five of these were number one and scored there for 40 of the year's 52 weeks. With Parker's management, Arnold continued to dominate, with 13 of the 20 best-scoring country music songs of 1947\u20131948.<ref name=\"cmenc\" /> He became the host of [[Mutual Broadcasting System|Mutual Radio]]'s Purina-sponsored segment of the ''Opry'' and of Mutual's ''Checkerboard Jamboree'', a midday program shared with [[Ernest Tubb]] that was broadcast from a Nashville theater.<ref name=\"tubb\">{{cite book|last=Pugh|first=Ronnie|title=Ernest Tubb: The Texas Troubadour|publisher=Duke University Press|year=1998|isbn=978-0-8223-2190-3}}<!--|access-date=July 15, 2009--></ref> Recorded radio programs increased Arnold's popularity, as did the [[CBS Radio]] series ''Hometown Reunion'' with the [[Duke of Paducah]]. Arnold quit the Opry during 1948, and his ''Hometown Reunion'' briefly broadcast in competition with the Opry on Saturday nights. In 1949 and 1950, he performed in the Columbia movies ''[[Feudin' Rhythm]]'' and ''[[Hoedown (film)|Hoedown]].''\n\nArnold began working for television in the early 1950s, hosting ''[[The Eddy Arnold Show]]''. The summer program was broadcast successively by all three television networks, replacing the [[Perry Como]] and [[The Dinah Shore Show|Dinah Shore]] programs.<ref>{{Cite book|first1=Tim|last1=Brooks|first2=Earle|last2=Marsh|title=The Complete Directory to Prime Time Network TV Shows|publisher=Ballantine Books|year=1992|isbn=0-345-37792-3}}</ref> He also performed as a guest and a [[guest host]] on the [[American Broadcasting Company|ABC-TV]] show ''[[Ozark Jubilee]]'' from 1955 to 1960.<ref>Weekly program listings (1955\u20131960), Triangle Publications ''[[TV Guide]]'', Vols. 3\u20138</ref> Arnold featured in the syndicated ''[[Eddy Arnold Time]]'' from 1955 to 1957.<ref name=\"Streissguth1997\" /> From 1960 to 1961, he hosted [[NBC|NBC-TV]]'s ''[[Today on the Farm]]''.<ref>\n{{Cite book|first=Alex|last=McNeil|title=Total Television|publisher=Penguin Books|year=1996|isbn=0-14-024916-8}}</ref>\n\n== Second career: The Nashville sound ==\nWith the rise of [[rock and roll]] in the mid 1950s, Arnold's record sales began to decline, though fellow RCA Victor country recording artist [[Jim Reeves]] found a greater audience with popular-sounding string-laced arrangements. Arnold annoyed many in the country music establishment by recording with [[Hugo Winterhalter]] and his Orchestra at the [[RCA Studios New York#24th St|RCA Victor Studios]] in New York. Winterhalter's pop-oriented arrangements of \"[[The Cattle Call]]\" and \"The Richest Man (in the World)\", however, helped to expand Arnold's appeal beyond its country music base.<ref name=\"encm\">{{cite book|last=Rumble|first=John|title=The Encyclopedia of Country Music|url=https://archive.org/details/encyclopediaofco00coun|url-access=registration|editor=Paul Kingsbury|publisher=Oxford University Press|year=1998|isbn=978-0-19-511671-7}}</ref> This style, pioneered by Reeves and Arnold, became known as the \"[[Nashville Sound]]\".<ref name=\"encm\" /> During 1953, Arnold and Tom Parker had a dispute, and Arnold fired him.<ref>{{cite book |last=Ward |first=Ed |date=2016 |title=The History of Rock & Roll, volume one, 1920\u20131963 \n|location=New York |publisher=Flatiron Books |page=103 |isbn=978-1-250-07116-3 |author-link=Ed Ward (writer)}}</ref> From 1954 to 1963, Arnold's performances were managed by Joe Csida; in 1964, Csida was replaced by Jerry Purcell.<ref name=\"skyline\">{{cite news|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1587136/nashville-skyline-remembering-eddy-arnold.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080512152607/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1587136/nashville-skyline-remembering-eddy-arnold.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=May 12, 2008|title=NASHVILLE SKYLINE: Remembering Eddy Arnold|last=Flippo|first=Chet|date=May 8, 2008|publisher=Country Music Television|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref>\n\nArnold embarked on a second career that brought his music to a more diverse audience. In the summer of 1965, he had his first number-one country song in 10 years, \"[[What's He Doing in My World]]\" and struck gold again six months later with the song that became his most well-known, \"[[Make the World Go Away]]\", accompanied by pianist [[Floyd Cramer]] on piano and featuring the [[Anita Kerr]] Singers. As a result, Arnold's rendition became an international success. \"Make The World Go Away\" became his only top ten pop hit.<ref name=\"encm\" />\n\nBill Walker's orchestra arrangements provided the lush background for 16 continuous successes sung by Arnold in the late 1960s. Arnold performed with [[orchestra|symphony orchestras]] in New York City, Las Vegas, and Hollywood. He performed in [[Carnegie Hall]] for two concerts, and in the Coconut Grove in Las Vegas.<ref name=\"encm\" /> In 1966, Arnold was inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame]], the youngest performer to receive the honor.<ref name=\"country music\">{{cite news|url=http://www.wickedlocal.com/norwich/entertainment/music/x647002031/Country-star-Eddy-Arnold-dies|title=Country legend Eddy Arnold dies|agency=Associated Press|date=May 8, 2008|publisher=[[MSNBC]]|access-date=July 15, 2009|archive-date=May 22, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200522001639/http://www.wickedlocal.com/norwich/entertainment/music/x647002031/Country-star-Eddy-Arnold-dies/|url-status=dead}}</ref> The following year, Arnold was voted the first-ever awarded [[Country Music Association]]'s Entertainer of the Year.<ref name=\"cmaawards\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/microsites/cma/archives/1967.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081021035600/http://www.cmt.com/microsites/cma/archives/1967.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=October 21, 2008|title=CMA Awards Ceremonies|year=2009|publisher=Country Music Association|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref> Two years later, he released an autobiography named ''It's A Long Way From Chester County''.<ref name=\"autobio\">{{cite book|last=Arnold|first=Eddy|title=It's A Long Way From Chester County|url=https://archive.org/details/itslongwayfromch00arno|url-access=registration|publisher=Hewitt House|location=Old Tappan, New Jersey|year=1969}}</ref>\n\nHaving been with RCA Victor since 1944, Arnold left the label in 1973 for [[MGM Records]], where he recorded four albums, which included several top-40 successes. He returned to RCA in 1976 and recorded for the company for the remainder of his career.<ref name=\"cmenc\" />\n\n== Later years and death ==\nDuring the 1980s, Arnold declared himself semi-retired, but he continued recording. In 1984, the [[Academy of Country Music]] awarded Arnold its Pioneer Award. His next album, ''You Don't Miss A Thing'', was not released until 1991.<ref name=\"cmenc\" /> Arnold performed road tours for several more years.<ref name=\"1991return\">{{cite news|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=RTEMAAAAIBAJ&pg=3056,1023370&dq=eddy+arnold|title=Eddy Arnold resumes his singing career|date=February 7, 1991|publisher=Saint Petersburg Times|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref> By 1992, he had sold nearly 85 million records, and had a total of 145 weeks of number-one songs, more than any other singer.<ref name=\"cmenc\" />\n[[File:Eddy_Arnold.jpg|thumb|upright|Arnold in 1998]]\nIn 1996, RCA issued an album of Arnold's main successes since 1944 as part of its 'Essential' series.<ref name=\"cmenc\" /> Arnold, then 78 years old, retired from active singing, though he still performed occasionally.<ref name=\"encm\" /> On May 16, 1998, the day after his 80th birthday, he announced his final retirement during a concert at the Hotel Orleans in Las Vegas.<ref name=\"retire\">{{cite news|title=Calling It Quits|last=Paskevich|first=Michael|date=May 14, 1999|work=Las Vegas Review-Journal}}</ref> That same year, the [[National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences]] inducted the recording of \"Make The World Go Away\" into the [[Grammy Hall of Fame]]. In 2000, he was awarded the [[National Medal of Arts]].<ref>[http://www.nea.gov/honors/medals/medalists_year.html#00 Lifetime Honors \u2013 National Medal of Arts] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110721054307/http://www.nea.gov/honors/medals/medalists_year.html |date=July 21, 2011 }}</ref> In 2005, Arnold received a [[Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award|Lifetime Achievement Award]] from the [[Recording Academy]],<ref name=\"laa\">{{cite news|url=https://www.usatoday.com/life/music/news/2005-01-05-lewis-lifetime_x.htm?POE=LIFISVA|title=Jerry Lee Lewis wins Achievement Award|agency=Associated Press|date=January 5, 2005|work=USA Today|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref> and later that year, released a final album for RCA titled ''After All These Years''.<ref name=\"gormly\">{{cite news|url=http://www.pittsburghlive.com/x/pittsburghtrib/s_379215.html|title=Arnold offers gem for traditionalists with 100th album|last=Gormly|first=Kellie B.|date=October 2, 2005|publisher=Pittsburgh Tribune-Review|access-date=July 15, 2009|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110101033334/http://www.pittsburghlive.com/x/pittsburghtrib/s_379215.html|archive-date=January 1, 2011}}</ref>\n\nArnold died from natural causes on May 8, 2008, in a care facility in Nashville, at age 89. His wife of 66 years, Sally Gayhart Arnold, had preceded him in death by two months. They are survived by two children (Richard E. Arnold, Jr., and JoAnn Arnold Pollard), two grandchildren (K. Michelle Pollard and R. Shannon Pollard, Jr.), and four great-grandchildren (Katie E. Pollard, Jack Pollard, Rowan Pollard, and Ben Johns).<ref name=\"may8death\">{{cite news|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1587054/country-music-hall-of-fame-member-eddy-arnold-dies-at-age-89.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080512152604/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1587054/country-music-hall-of-fame-member-eddy-arnold-dies-at-age-89.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=May 12, 2008|title=Country Music Hall of Fame Member Eddy Arnold Dies at Age 89|last=Pugh|first=Ronnie|date=May 8, 2008|publisher=Country Music Television|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref>\n\nOn May 31, 2008, RCA released \"To Life\" as a single from the album ''After All These Years''. It debuted at number 49 on the Hot Country Songs charts, Arnold's first entry in 25 years and the recording by the oldest person to chart in ''Billboard'' magazine. It set the record for the longest span between a first chart single and a last: 62 years and 11 months (\"Each Minute Seems Like a Million Years\" debuted on June 30, 1945), and extended Arnold's career chart history to seven decades.<ref name=\"arnold\">{{cite news|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1587711/eddy-arnolds-to-life-stretches-into-seventh-decade.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090116020513/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1587711/eddy-arnolds-to-life-stretches-into-seventh-decade.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=January 16, 2009|title=Eddy Arnold's \"To Life\" Stretches Chart Success Into Seventh Decade|date=May 19, 2008|publisher=Country Music Television|access-date=July 15, 2009}}</ref>\n\n== Discography This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Statler_Brothers","to":"The Statler Brothers"}],"pages":{"1024007":{"pageid":1024007,"ns":0,"title":"The Statler Brothers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American country music, gospel, and vocal group}}\n{{Use American English|date=February 2021}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=February 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist \n| name                 = The Statler Brothers\n| image                = File:Statler promo.jpg\n| image_size           = \n| caption              = A promotional image of the Statler Brothers, 1970s. From left to right: Harold Reid, Don Reid, Phil Balsley, and Lew DeWitt.\n| background           = group_or_band\n| alias                =\n* The Four Star Quartet\n* The Kingsmen\n| origin               = [[Staunton, Virginia]], U.S.\n| genre                = {{flatlist|\n* [[Country music|Country]]\n* [[Gospel music|gospel]]\n* [[southern gospel]]\n* [[traditional pop]]\n}}\n| years_active         = 1955\u20132002\n| label                = {{flatlist|\n* [[Columbia Records|Columbia]]\n* [[Mercury Records|Mercury]]\n* Music Box\n* Yell\n}}\n| website              = {{URL|thestatlerbrothers.com}}\n| past_members         = {{plainlist|\n* Joe McDorman\n* Don Reid\n* Harold Reid\n* Phil Balsley\n* [[Lew DeWitt]]\n* [[Jimmy Fortune]]\n}}\n}}\n'''The Statler Brothers''' (sometimes simply referred to as '''The Statlers''') were an American [[country music]], [[gospel music|gospel]], and vocal group from [[Staunton, Virginia]]. The quartet was formed in 1955 performing locally, and from 1964 to 1972, they sang as opening act and backup singers for [[Johnny Cash]].<ref>Mike Morsch, ''The Vinyl Dialogues: Stories Behind Memorable Albums of the 1970s as Told by the Artists'' (Biblio, 2014), pp. 73\u201376. {{ISBN|9781622492077}}</ref>\n\nOriginally performing [[Southern gospel]] music at local churches, the group billed themselves as The Four Star Quartet, and later The Kingsmen.<ref name=\"AmGosp\">{{cite encyclopedia\n | editor = W. K. McNeil\n | encyclopedia = Encyclopedia of Gospel Music\n | title = The Statler Brothers\n | year = 2005\n | publisher = Routledge\n | location = Glasgow\n | isbn = 0-415-94179-2\n | pages = 376\n}}</ref> In 1963, when the song \"[[Louie, Louie]]\" by the [[garage rock]] band also called [[The Kingsmen]] became famous, the group elected to bill themselves as the Statler Brothers.  Despite the name, only two members of the group (Don and Harold Reid) were actual brothers and no member had the surname of Statler. The group actually named themselves after a brand of [[facial tissue]] they had noticed in a hotel room (they later quipped that they could just as easily have named themselves \"the [[Kleenex]] Brothers\").<ref name=\"Stamler\">{{cite encyclopedia\n | editor = Irwin Stamler & Grelund Landon\n | encyclopedia = Country Music: The Encyclopedia\n | title = The Statler Brothers\n | year = 1997\n | publisher = Macmillan\n | location = New York\n | isbn = 0-312-26487-9\n | pages = 459\n}}</ref> Don Reid sang [[lead singer|lead]]; Harold Reid, Don's older brother, sang [[Bass (voice type)|bass]]; Phil Balsley sang [[baritone]]; and [[Lew DeWitt]] sang [[tenor]] and was the [[guitarist]] before being replaced due to ill health by [[Jimmy Fortune]] in 1981.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://countrymusichalloffame.org/artist/the-statler-brothers/ |title=The Statler Brothers |publisher=[[Country Music Hall of Fame]]}}</ref>\n\nThe band's style was closely linked to their gospel roots. \"We took gospel harmonies,\" said Harold Reid, \"and put them over in country music.\"<ref name=\"AmGosp\" /> Most of their albums contain at least one gospel song, and they produced several containing only gospel. They also recorded a tribute song to [[The Blackwood Brothers]], who influenced their music. The song \"We Got Paid by Cash\" was written by the Statler Brothers as a tribute to Johnny Cash, who discovered and mentored them.<ref name=\"AmGosp\" />\n\n== Career ==\nEarly in the group's history, before the group named themselves The Statler Brothers, Joe McDorman was their lead singer.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/1985/11/17/lew-dewitt-after-illness-and-despair-a-statler-brother-makes/|title=Lew Dewitt: After Illness And Despair, A Statler Brother Makes|date=November 17, 1985 |url-status=live|archive-url=http://archive.wikiwix.com/cache/20140109112845/http://articles.chicagotribune.com/1985-11-17/entertainment/8503190341_1_jimmy-fortune-phil-balsley-harold-reid|archive-date=January 9, 2014}}</ref>\n\nThe Statlers began their career at a performance at Lyndhurst Methodist Church near their hometown of Staunton, Virginia, under the name The Four Star Quartet.<ref name=\"AmGosp\" /> In 1964, they started an eight-year run as Johnny Cash's opening act and backing vocalists.<ref name=\"Stamler\" /> This period of their career was memorialized in their song \"We Got Paid by Cash.\" They were featured regularly on ''[[The Johnny Cash Show]]'', his [[American Broadcasting Company|ABC]] hit show that ran from 1969 to 1971. Due to their expanding career, the Statlers left Cash's entourage around the mid-1970s to concentrate on their own career, a departure that took place on good terms.\n\nTwo of the Statlers' best-known songs are \"[[Flowers on the Wall]],\" their first major hit that was composed and written by Lew DeWitt, and the socially conscious \"[[Bed of Rose's]]\". In the 1980s, the Statlers were a mainstay on [[Spike TV|The Nashville Network (TNN)]], where their videos were shown regularly. Also on TNN, between 1991 and 1998, they hosted ''[[The Statler Brothers Show]]'', a weekly [[variety show]], which was the network's top-rated program for its entire 7-year run.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.gmacanada.ca/go/site/news/2007/09/ |title=Biography |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071214092844/http://www.gmacanada.ca/go/site/news/2007/09/ |archive-date=December 14, 2007 |website=Rex Allen, Jr.'s official website |access-date=April 18, 2008}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/news/ct-xpm-1995-01-07-9501070171-story.html |title=Statler Bros.' TNN Show Still Going Strong |first=Shirley |last=Jinkins |newspaper=Chicago Tribune via Ft. Worth Star-Telegram |date=January 7, 1995 |access-date=June 1, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.tampabay.com/archive/1996/01/05/statler-bros-begin-fifth-year-on-tnn/ |title=Statler Bros. begin fifth year on TNN |first=Jean |last=Prescot |newspaper=Tampa Bay Times |date=September 15, 2005 |access-date=June 1, 2020}}</ref>\n\nThroughout the Statlers' career, much of their appeal was related to their incorporation of comedy and parody into their musical act, due in large part to the humorous and comedic talent of group member Harold Reid; they were frequently nominated for awards for their comedy as well as their singing. They recorded two comedy albums under the [[pseudonym]] Lester \"Roadhog\" Moran and the Cadillac Cowboys, and one-half of one side of the album ''Country Music Then and Now'' was devoted to satirizing small-town radio stations' Saturday-morning shows.\n\nThe Statlers earned the number-one spot on the [[Billboard charts|''Billboard'' chart]] four times, for \"[[Do You Know You Are My Sunshine]]?\" in 1978, \"[[Elizabeth (The Statler Brothers song)|Elizabeth]]\" in 1984, and in 1985, \"[[My Only Love (song)|My Only Love]]\" and \"[[Too Much on My Heart]].\"<ref name=\"CMT\">{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/statler_brothers/bio.jhtml |title=Artist Biography: The Statler Brothers |access-date=April 17, 2008 |work=[[Country Music Television]] |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080325074504/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/statler_brothers/bio.jhtml |archive-date=March 25, 2008}}</ref> Since forming, the Statlers have released over 40 albums.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://thestatlerbrothers.com/discography/ |title=Discography |website=The Statler Brothers' Official website |access-date=June 1, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://statlerbrothers.com/ |title=The Statlers |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080509155220/http://statlerbrothers.com/ |archive-date=May 9, 2008 |access-date=April 10, 2008}}</ref>\n\nIn 1980, the Statler Brothers purchased and renovated their former elementary school, Beverly Manor, in Staunton, occupying the complex for several years. The complex consisted of offices for the group, a small museum and auditorium, and an adjacent building that served as office space for unrelated businesses. A garage was built to store the two tour buses that the group had used for many years. The group has since sold the complex, which Grace Christian Church in Staunton converted back into an academic campus.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.gcswarriors.org/contact-us/directions.cfm |title=Elementary/Middle School Directions |website=Grace Christian School |access-date=June 1, 2020}}</ref>\n\nIn 1970, the group began performing at an annual [[Independence Day (United States)|Independence Day]] festival in Gypsy Hill Park in Staunton. The event, known as \"Happy Birthday USA,\" lasted for 25 years, and included many country-music figures, including [[Mel Tillis]], [[Charley Pride]], and many others. The event drew as many as 100,000 fans each year. The group also honored their hometown with the song \"Staunton, Virginia\" on their 1973 album ''Do You Love Me Tonight''.\n\nDeWitt retired from the Statler Brothers in 1982 due to ill health. After a 3-year hiatus, he returned to the music industry as a solo artist until shortly before his death on August 15, 1990, from complications of [[Crohn's disease]], at age 52.<ref>[https://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9C0CE0D9133EF934A2575BC0A966958260 \"Lew DeWitt, 52, Tenor With the Statler Brothers\"]. ''[[The New York Times]]'' (obituary). (August 17, 1990) retrieved April 10, 2008.</ref>\n\nHarold Reid (born on August 21, 1939<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/59247685/the-news-leader/|title=Clipped from the News Leader|newspaper=The News Leader|date=August 22, 1939|page=3}}</ref>) died on April 24, 2020, after a long battle with kidney failure, at age 80.<ref>[https://eu.newsleader.com/story/news/local/2020/04/24/harold-reid-founding-member-statler-brothers-dies-80/3013597001/  Brad Zinn, \"Harold Reid, founding member of Statler Brothers, dies at 80\", ''News Leader'', April 25, 2020]. Retrieved April 25, 2020</ref><ref name=mfh>{{cite news|url=https://www.henryfuneralhome.net/obituaries/Harold-Reid-4/#!/Obituary|title=Harold Reid August 21, 1939 - April 24, 2020 Obituary|publisher=henryfuneralhome.net|access-date=August 7, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.newsleader.com/story/news/local/2020/04/24/harold-reid-founding-member-statler-brothers-dies-80/3013597001/|title=Harold Reid, founding member of Statler Brothers, dies at 80 |last=Zinn|first=Brad|website=The News Leader|language=en|access-date=April 25, 2020}}</ref>\n\n== Awards ==\n'''[[Academy of Country Music]]'''\n* 1972 Top Vocal Group\n* 1977 Top Vocal Group\n* 2016 Cliffie Stone Pioneer Award\n\n'''[[Country Music Association]]'''\n* [[Country Music Association Awards|1972 Vocal Group of the Year]]\n* 1973 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1974 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1975 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1976 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1977 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1979 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1980 Vocal Group of the Year\n* 1984 Vocal Group of the Year\n\n'''[[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum]]'''\n* Inducted in 2008<ref>[https://www.usatoday.com/life/music/2008-06-27-2717453777_x.htm \"Statler Brothers: Country Hall of Fame Honor Tops\"] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110702143033/http://www.usatoday.com/life/music/2008-06-27-2717453777_x.htm |date=July 2, 2011 }}. (undated). Retrieved March 29, 2008.</ref>\n\n'''[[American Music Awards]]'''\n* Favorite Country Band, Duo or Group 1979\n* Favorite Country Band, Duo or Group 1980\n* Favorite Country Band, Duo or Group 1981\n\n== Retirement ==\nThe group disbanded and retired after completing a farewell tour on October 26, 2002. Balsley and Don Reid continue to reside in Staunton, as did Harold Reid until his death in April 2020;  Fortune, though, relocated to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]], where he continues his music career as a solo artist, having released three albums under his own name. The Statlers remain one of the most awarded acts in the history of country music.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://countrymusic.about.com/od/statlerbrother1/a/statlerbrosbio.htm |title=About the Statler Brothers |first=Kathy |last=Coleman |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070905034239/http://countrymusic.about.com/od/statlerbrother1/a/statlerbrosbio.htm |archive-date=September 5, 2007 |url-status=dead |website=about.com |access-date=April 13, 2008}}</ref>\n\nDon Reid has pursued a second career as an author, having written six books of his own. With his sons Donald II (\"Debo\") and Langdon, he co-wrote ''You Know It's Christmas When . . .'' His brother Harold and he co-wrote a history of the Statler Brothers titled ''Random Memories'', published in February 2008. In 2020, Reid wrote a complete anthology of the Statlers' songs, titled ''The Music of the Statler Brothers.''<ref>Reid, Don. 2020. ''The Music of the Statler Brothers.'' Mercer University Press.</ref>\n\n== Grandstaff/Wilson Fairchild ==\nWil and Langdon Reid, the sons of Harold and Don, respectively, formed a duo in the 1990s, originally performing under the name Grandstaff.  In 2007, Grandstaff recorded \"The Statler Brothers Song\" as a tribute to the Statlers.\n\nIn an interview on Nashville's [[WSM (AM)]] on March 25, 2010, Wil Reid said that they decided to change their name to Wilson Fairchild after many people got the name \"Grandstaff\" wrong during introductions.  The name comes from \"Wilson,\" Wil's middle name, and \"Fairchild,\" Langdon's middle name.\n\nSisters Kim and Karmen Reid (daughters of Harold) also enjoyed a brief stint as a country duo in the early 1980s, which included a guest appearance on an episode of ''[[Hee Haw]]''.\n\n== Influence ==\nThe Statler Brothers have been credited as the first country music act to transfer the genre's nostalgia from a rural to a suburban setting.<ref name=\"CMT\" /> They have also been called \"America's Poets\" by [[Kurt Vonnegut]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.birthplaceofcountrymusic.org/node/1533|title=Blue Ridge PBS features Statler Brothers Farewell Concert|access-date=April 17, 2008|publisher=Birthplace of Country Music|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080605055855/http://www.birthplaceofcountrymusic.org/node/1533|archive-date=June 5, 2008}}</ref> The [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]] duo [[Dailey & Vincent]] often performs with two other members of their band as a quartet in the style of the Statlers, often performing many of the Statlers' hits in their shows. Jimmy Fortune also sometimes tours with Dailey & Vincent.\n\n==Members and years active==\n*Joe McDorman \u2013 lead (1955\u20131960)\n*[[Lew DeWitt]] \u2013 tenor (1955\u20131982) (died 1990)\n*Phil Balsley \u2013 baritone (1955\u20132002)\n*Harold Reid \u2013 bass (1955\u20132002) (died 2020)\n*Don Reid \u2013 lead (1960\u20132002)\n*[[Jimmy Fortune]] \u2013 tenor (1982\u20132002)\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|The Statler Brothers discography}}\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dae8Bt3xl0s The Statler Brothers performing at the Grand ole Opry in 1972]\n* [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UmDpqWuhuXc The Statler Brothers performing a gospel in the Johnny Cash Show during the 1960s]\n* [http://www.statlerbrothers.com/ Official Website]\n* [https://web.archive.org/web/20040203111303/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/statler_brothers/artist.jhtml at CMT]\n* [http://jimmyfortune.com/ Jimmy Fortune's Homepage]\n\n{{The Statler Brothers}}\n{{2000s Country Music Hall of Fame}}\n{{American Music Award for Favorite Country Band/Duo/Group}}\n{{CMA Group of the Year}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Statler Brothers}}\n[[Category:Country music groups from Virginia]]\n[[Category:Country Music Hall of Fame inductees]]\n[[Category:Grammy Award winners]]\n[[Category:Musical groups from Virginia]]\n[[Category:Vocal quartets]]\n[[Category:Musical groups established in 1955]]\n[[Category:Musical groups disestablished in 2002]]\n[[Category:Columbia Records artists]]\n[[Category:Mercury Records artists]]\n[[Category:1955 establishments in Virginia]]\n[[Category:2002 disestablishments in Virginia]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes.
