This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Stella_Parton","to":"Stella Parton"}],"pages":{"2577538":{"pageid":2577538,"ns":0,"title":"Stella Parton","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country singer (born 1949)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=October 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Stella Parton\n| image           = Stella Parton, smiling.jpg\n| caption         = Autographed photo of Stella Parton; late 1970s\n| image_size      = \n| birth_name      = Stella Mae Parton\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1949|5|4}}\n| birth_place     = [[Sevierville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| genre           = {{Hlist|[[Country music|Country]]|[[Gospel music|gospel]]}}\n| occupation      = Singer, songwriter\n| years_active    = 1967\u2013present\n| label           = [[Elektra Records|Elektra]]<br />{{nowrap|Soul, Country and Blues}}<br />Raptor\n| website         = {{URL|stellaparton.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Stella Mae Parton''' (born May 4, 1949)<ref name=\"LarkinGE\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Encyclopedia of Popular Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1992|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-939-0|page=1916}}</ref> is an American [[Country music|country]] singer and songwriter widely known for a series of country singles that charted during the mid-to-late-1970s, her biggest hit being \"I Want to Hold You in My Dreams Tonight\" in 1975.<ref name=\"Stella Parton\">{{cite book|last=Parton|first=Stella|title=Tell It Sister, Tell It|year=2011|publisher=Attic Entertainment|isbn=978-0-615-44314-0|pages=223}}</ref><ref name=\"Stella Parton Billboard\">{{cite web |title=Stella Parton Billboard |url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/stella-parton/chart-history/csi/ |website=Billboard.com |access-date=June 14, 2021}}</ref> She is a younger sister of singer-songwriter [[Dolly Parton]] and an older sister of the late [[Randy Parton]] and former actress [[Rachel Dennison|Rachel Parton George]].\n\n== Early life ==\nParton was born in [[Sevierville, Tennessee]],<ref name=\"LarkinGE\" /> the sixth of 12 children born to Avie Lee Caroline (''[[n\u00e9e]]'' Owens; 1923\u20132003) and Robert Lee Parton Sr. (1921\u20132000). Dolly Parton is her elder sister by three years.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.smokykin.com/ged/f004/f84/a0048420.htm |title=Pedigree Chart for Rachel Ann Parton: Smoky Mountain Ancestral Quest |website=Smoky Kin |date=April 4, 201 |access-date=April 18, 2012}}</ref> When Stella was seven, she and Dolly appeared on a [[Knoxville, Tennessee|Knoxville]] television program, and two years later she debuted on radio. During this time, Stella and her sisters Willadeene and Cassie formed a group who sang [[gospel music]] and made commercials around [[East Tennessee]]. During her high school years, she began writing songs. She married Marvin Carroll Rauhuff just before her high school graduation in 1966. She had one son by this marriage.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.smokykin.com/tng/getperson.php?personID=I48414&tree=smokykin |title=Stella Mae Parton b. 4 May 1949 d.|website=Smoky Kin |quote= Stella Parton marries Marvin Rauhuff|access-date=February 23, 2009}}</ref>\n\n== Recording career ==\nIn 1967, Parton released her first album, ''In the Garden'' (a gospel project with Willadeene, Cassie and their mother). Shortly thereafter, she moved to Washington, D.C., and began performing at the Hillbilly Heaven club. Later moving to Nashville, she started her own record label, Soul, Country and Blues, in 1975 and released her first solo album, ''I Want to Hold You in My Dreams Tonight''. Its title track was a substantial national hit, climbing into the country top ten.<ref name=\"Stella Parton Billboard\" /> Its success earned her a major-label deal with Elektra in 1976.<ref name=\"LarkinGE\" /> Her 1977 duet with Carmol Taylor, \"Neon Woman\", was somewhat successful, and she had three top 20 hits over 1977\u20131978 with \"The Danger of a Stranger\" (also a top 40 hit in the UK), \"Four Little Letters\" and \"Standard Lie Number One\".<ref name=\"LarkinGE\" /> She had an additional top-40 hit with her sister Dolly's composition, \"Steady as the Rain\", in 1979.<ref name=\"Stella Parton Billboard\" /> She recorded three albums for Elektra up to 1979. In 1984, Stella performed a song with Kin Vassey for the soundtrack of the movie ''[[Rhinestone (film soundtrack)|Rhinestone]]'', in which Dolly starred.<ref name=\"LarkinGE\" />\n\nThough her chart success tapered off after leaving Elektra in 1980, she continued to record, releasing albums for several independent labels, including Accord/Townhouse and Airborne. She is currently{{when|date=July 2021}} with Raptor Records. To date,{{when|date=July 2021}} she has released 22 albums and has had 28 charting singles.\n\nParton has released a DVD, ''Live in Nashville'', of footage from a 1990 concert in Nashville taken from the Attic Entertainment archives. It is the first of a planned Vintage Collection Series.\n\nIn 2019, Parton released an album, ''Survivor''. In addition to eight original songs, ''Survivor'' has a cover version of \"[[Wake Me Up (Avicii song)|Wake Me Up]]\" by [[Avicii]] and Parton's interpretation of the [[Bob Seger]] classic, \"[[Like a Rock (song)|Like a Rock]]\".<ref>{{cite web |last1=Whitmore |first1=Laura |title=Exclusive Premiere: Stella Parton Shares Inspiring Video for 'Like A Rock' from New Album Survivor |url=https://parade.com/865445/laurawhitmore/exclusive-premiere-stella-parton-shares-inspiring-video-for-like-a-rock-from-new-album-survivor/ |website=Parade |date=March 28, 2019 |access-date=June 14, 2021}}<br />- {{cite web |last1=Stefano |first1=Angela |title=Stella Parton, 'Dirty Rotten Dog' Music Video [Premiere] |url=https://theboot.com/stella-parton-dirty-rotten-dog-music-video/ |website=The Boot|date=March 2019 |access-date=June 14, 2021}}</ref>\n\n== Television and film work ==\nIn 1970, Parton appeared on The Porter Wagoner Show. Parton performed George Hamilton IV's \"Break My Mind\" with sisters Dolly and Cassie. She performed \"Cotton Fields\" later in the show.\n\nIn 1979, Parton starred in ''[[The Dukes of Hazzard]]'' episode titled \"Deputy Dukes\" as Mary Beth Malone, a woman who impersonates a police officer to settle a family score with a prisoner who ends up being transported by Bo ([[John Schneider (screen actor)|John Schneider]]) and Luke ([[Tom Wopat]]) during a change of venue.\n\nDuring the 1980s and early 1990s, she starred in several Broadway touring musicals, including ''[[Seven Brides for Seven Brothers (musical)|Seven Brides for Seven Brothers]]'', ''[[Pump Boys & Dinettes]]'', ''[[Best Little Whorehouse In Texas]]'' and ''[[Gentlemen Prefer Blondes (musical)|Gentlemen Prefer Blondes]]''. Parton also wrote and staged several [[Dollywood]] shows the opening season, as well as appearing on ''The Dukes of Hazzard'' (the first country artist to have a dramatic role on the series), ''[[Live with Regis and Kathy Lee]]'', ''[[Today (NBC program)|The Today Show]]'' and ''[[Good Morning America]]''. She has been on several international radio programs, including ''Get Focused Radio'' with host Kate Hennessy.\n\nParton appeared with [[Gena Rowlands]] and [[Louis Gossett]] in the 2000 TV movie ''The Color of Love: Jacey's Story'' which was nominated for a Primetime Emmy award.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Color of Love: Jacey's Story (TV movie 2000) |url=https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0219695/ |website=IMDb |date=March 19, 2000 |access-date=June 14, 2021}}</ref>\n\nIn 2006, Parton made appearances in two films, ''A Dance for Bethany'' and ''Ghost Town'', both scheduled for release in 2007. Each film also includes her music on the soundtrack. Also ready for release in 2007 was her 21st album, which is a collection of original contemporary Christian songs. Followed in 2008, was her 22nd album, ''[[Testimony (Stella Parton album)|Testimony]]''.<ref name=\"Stella Parton\" />\n\nShe appeared in ''[[Dolly Parton's Coat of Many Colors]]'' with [[Jennifer Nettles]] and [[Ricky Schroder]],<ref>{{cite web |title=Dolly Parton's Coat of Many Colors (TV movie 2015) \u2013 Full Cast & Crew \u2013 IMDb |url=https://www.imdb.com/title/tt4767274/fullcredits |website=IMDb |access-date=June 14, 2021}}</ref> an [[NBC]] made-for-TV movie based on Dolly's song of the same name that was first broadcast on [[NBC]] in December 2015.\n\nIn 2016, Parton appeared in ''[[Dolly Parton's Christmas of Many Colors: Circle of Love]]'' as Corla Bass. The [[NBC]] TV movie was nominated for a [[Primetime Emmy]] award for Outstanding Television Movie.<ref>{{cite web |title=Dolly Parton's Christmas of Many Colors: Circle of Love (TV Movie 2016) |url=https://www.imdb.com/title/tt5713426/ |website=IMDb |date=November 30, 2016 |access-date=June 14, 2021}}</ref>\n\nIn 2018, she took part in the BBC's ''[[Celebrity Masterchef]]'' series.<ref>{{cite news |title=Celebrity MasterChef: Dolly Parton's sister in line-up|work= BBC News|date= May 16, 2018|url= https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-44104497|access-date=December 24, 2023}}</ref>\n\nShe appeared as a mystery guest on ''[[To Tell the Truth]]'' hosted by [[Anthony Anderson]] in 2021, and none of the panelists guessed her as the real sibling of Dolly Parton.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Bhattacharjee |first1=Debopriya |title=Dolly Parton's Sister has Made Quite a Wave on 'To Tell The Truth'|website=The CineTalk |url=https://thecinetalk.com/2021/04/11/dolly-partons-sister-has-made-quite-a-wave-on-to-tell-the-truth-read-on-to-know-more/|access-date=June 14, 2021}}</ref>\n\nIn 2022 she appeared in the [[Pure Flix]] film ''Nothing is Impossible'', starring [[David A.R. White]], which was filmed in Tennessee.\n\n== Social work ==\nShe devotes much of her time to causes such as domestic violence and teaches at the New Opportunity School for Women at [[Berea College]], Kentucky, using her knowledge of hair and make-up to help women build self-esteem.\n\nParton has been a national spokesperson for [[Mothers Against Drunk Driving]] and the [[Christian Appalachian Project]] and National Honorary Country Music Ambassador to the American Cancer Society.<ref name=\"Stella Parton\" />\n\nParton went viral on ''Twitter'' in December 2020 with a tweet criticizing \"old moldy politicians\" over the sluggish COVID-19 vaccine rollout in the United States.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Folley |first1=Aris |title=Stella Parton, singer and sister of Dolly, lashes out at politicians in viral tweet over COVID-19 vaccine rollout |url=https://thehill.com/blogs/in-the-know/in-the-know/531073-stella-parton-singer-and-sister-of-dolly-lashes-out-at |website=The Hill |date=December 20, 2020 |access-date=June 18, 2021}}</ref>\n\n== Other ventures ==\nParton has a consulting business, Attic Entertainment Artist Development and Entertainment Consulting, which teaches stage presence, hair, make-up, wardrobe techniques and video coaching. She has also written three cookbooks, including  ''State Fairs and Church Bazaars''.<ref name=\"Stella Parton\" />\n\n== Discography ==\n{{Main|Stella Parton discography}}\n{{div col}}\n*''In the (1931-1999)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name         = Boxcar Willie\n| image        = Boxcar_Willie.jpg\n| caption      = Martin in Boxcar Willie garb\n| birth_name   = Lecil Travis Martin\n| alias        = Boxcar Willie\n| birth_date   = {{birth date|1931|09|01}}\n| birth_place  = [[Ovilla, Texas]], U.S.\n| death_date   = {{Death date and age|1999|04|12|1931|09|01}}\n| death_place  = [[Branson, Missouri]], U.S.\n| instrument   = Vocals, guitar, [[train whistle]]\n| genre        = [[Country music|Country]], [[Gospel music|gospel]]\n| occupation   = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active =\n| website      = [http://www.boxcarwillie.com/ www.boxcarwillie.com]\n| module       = {{Infobox military person|embed=yes\n| allegiance    = United States\n| branch        = {{air force|United States}}\n| serviceyears  = 1949\u20131976\n| rank          = [[Master sergeant]] E7<ref>{{cite web | url=http://airforce.togetherweserved.com/usaf/servlet/tws.webapp.WebApp?cmd=ShadowBoxProfile&type=BattleMemoryExt&ID=42486 | title=Martin, Lecil Travis, MSgt | website=Weservedtogether.com | access-date=September 6, 2015 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304083757/http://airforce.togetherweserved.com/usaf/servlet/tws.webapp.WebApp?cmd=ShadowBoxProfile&type=BattleMemoryExt&ID=42486 | archive-date=March 4, 2016 | url-status=dead }}</ref>\n| battles       = [[Korean War]]\n| awards        =\n}}\n}}\n\n'''Lecil Travis Martin''' (September 1, 1931 \u2013 April 12, 1999), whose stage name was '''Boxcar Willie''', was an American [[country music]] singer-songwriter, who sang in the [[Hobo#Songs|\"old-time hobo\"]] music style, complete with overalls, and a floppy hat.<ref>Malone, Bill C. [https://books.google.com/books?id=CR63ED_FH_AC&pg=PA277 ''Country music, U.S.A.''], University of Texas Press, 2002, p. 277.</ref> \"Boxcar Willie\" was originally a character in a ballad he wrote, but he later adopted it as his own stage name.<ref>Mazor, Barry. [https://archive.org/details/meetingjimmierod00mazo/page/291 ''Meeting Jimmie Rodgers: How America's Original Roots Music Hero Changed the Pop Sounds of a Century''], [[Oxford University Press]], 2009, p. 291</ref> His early musical career was parallel to service as an enlisted [[flight engineer]] in the [[United States Air Force]].\n\n==Biography==\n{{more citations needed|section|date=January 2023}}\nAccording to his birth record, Martin was born in [[Ovilla, Texas]], to Birdie and Edna Mae Martin. He joined the [[United States Air Force]] in May 1949, and served as a [[flight engineer]] on the [[B-29 Super Fortress]] during the [[Korean War]] in the early 1950s. In [[Lincoln, Nebraska]], Martin was once sitting at a railroad crossing and a fellow that closely resembled his chief boom operator, Willie Wilson, passed by sitting in a [[boxcar]]. He said, \"There goes Willie.\" He pulled over and wrote a song entitled \"Boxcar Willie\".{{Citation needed|date=November 2008}} It eventually stuck and became Martin's nickname. In 1962, Martin met his future wife, Lloene, in [[Boise, Idaho]]. They later had four children.\n\nIn [[San Jose, California]], Martin attended a talent show as \"Boxcar Willie\" and performed under that nickname for the first time. He won first place and a $150 prize. That was his part-time vocation, however, as he was still in the Air Force and had been flying daily missions. In the early 1970s, while assigned to the [[181st Airlift Squadron|136th Air Refueling Wing]] of the [[Texas Air National Guard]], Martin served as a flight engineer aboard the [[Boeing KC-97 Stratofreighter]] and participated in Operation Creek Party. This operation provided critical in-flight refueling services for fighter aircraft assigned to the [[United States Air Forces in Europe]] for 10 years.\n\nIn 1976, Martin retired from the Air Force and became a full-time performer. One of his first national appearances was a win on [[Chuck Barris]]' ''[[The Gong Show]]''. In the late 1970s, Martin traveled to [[Grand Prairie, Texas]], where he purchased hundreds of [[8-track tape]]s pre-recorded with his music to sell later in various places. After he received a contract with other recording studios, he discontinued his dealings with Cleo McDonald.{{Context inline|date=January 2023}}\n\nMartin entered American mainstream pop culture consciousness due to a series of television commercials for record compilations of artists who were obscure in the United States, yet had large international followings, such as [[Slim Whitman]] and [[Gheorghe Zamfir]]. Martin went on to become a star in [[country music]]. In 1981, Martin achieved a professional landmark by being inducted into the ''[[Grand Ole Opry]]''.<ref name=\"Larkin\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Virgin Encyclopedia of Popular Music]]|editor=Colin Larkin|editor-link=Colin Larkin (writer)|publisher=[[Virgin Books]]|date=1997|edition=Concise|isbn=1-85227-745-9|page=171}}</ref> He also had success outside of the United States, with his 1980 album ''King of the Road'' giving him his greatest chart success by reaching No. 5 in the [[UK Albums Chart]].<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David| last= Roberts| year= 2006| title= [[British Hit Singles & Albums]]| edition= 19th| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited | location= London| isbn= 1-904994-10-5| page= 74}}</ref> Traveling around the world with Martin's band was his steadfast and trusty steel guitar player Chubby Howard, radio show host and musician for many years.\n\nIn 1985, Martin moved to [[Branson, Missouri]], and purchased a theater on [[Missouri Route 76]], also known as 76 Country Boulevard. In addition to the Boxcar Willie Theater, he opened a museum and eventually had two motels, both bearing his name. Martin was one of the first big stars to open a show in Branson, paving the way for the other nationally known names that followed.<ref name=\"salonobit\">[http://www.salon.com/people/obit/1999/04/14/boxcar/ \"BoxCar Willie\"] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20041107052516/http://www.salon.com/people/obit/1999/04/14/boxcar/ |date=November 7, 2004 }}, ''Salon'' obituary, April 14, 1999.</ref> He performed at his theater in Branson until his death.\n\nOn February 23, 1992, Martin was featured on the second-season premier of ''[[Tracks Ahead]]'' in which he performed with his band at the Boxcar Willie Theater.\n\n==Death==\nMartin was diagnosed with [[leukemia]] in 1996, and died on April 12, 1999, in [[Branson, Missouri]] at the age of 67. He was buried at Ozarks Memorial Park in Branson.<ref>{{cite book|last=Jasinski|first=Laurie E.|title=Handbook of Texas Music|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=CE8xiT3pV6QC&pg=PT239|year=2012|publisher=Texas State Historical Assn|isbn=978-0-87611-297-7|page=239}}</ref> [[Major League Baseball]] umpire [[Joe West (umpire)|\"Cowboy\" Joe West]] was among his pallbearers.\n\n==Legacy==\nAfter a major reconstruction project, the overpass carrying [[Farm to Market Road 664]] (locally known as Ovilla Road) over [[Interstate 35E (Texas)|Interstate 35E]] in [[Red Oak, Texas]], was renamed the Boxcar Willie Memorial Overpass. A small park, two blocks from the [[National Mall]], near the [[L'Enfant Plaza station]] in Washington, D.C., was renamed Boxcar Willie Park. Martin is still recalled by his nickname, \"America's Favorite Hobo\".<ref>{{cite news |url=http://wrvhs.org/announcements/tuesday-talk-americas-favorite-hobo/ |title=Tuesday Talk: America's Favorite Hobo |publisher=White River Valley Historical Society |website=wrvhs.org |date=January 16, 2023 |accessdate=January 28, 2023}}</ref> One of his sons, Larry Martin, has performed professionally under the stage name of Boxcar Willie Jr.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.101highlandlakes.com/news/boxcar-willie-tribute-lantex-theater |title=Boxcar Willie Jr. paying tribute to late father at LanTex Theater |website=101highlandlakes.com |date=September 9, 2015 |accessdate=January 28, 2023}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Year\n! rowspan=\"2\"| {{URL|freddiehart.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Frederick Segrest''' (December 21, 1926<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=183}}</ref> \u2013 October 27, 2018),<ref name=\"Obit\"/> known professionally as '''Freddie Hart''', was an American [[country music]]ian and songwriter best known for his [[chart-topper|chart-topping]] country song and [[one-hit wonder|lone pop hit]] \"[[Easy Loving]],\" which won the [[Country Music Association]] Song of the Year award in 1971 and 1972.<ref name=\"CMAawards\">[http://www.cmaawards.com/2007/database/ArtistDetail.aspx?artistId=87 CMA Awards Database \u2013 Freddie Hart] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090322160222/http://www.cmaawards.com/2007/database/ArtistDetail.aspx?artistId=87 |date=March 22, 2009 }}, Cmaawards.com; retrieved July 25, 2008</ref>\n\nHart charted singles from 1953 to 1987, and later became a [[gospel music|gospel]] singer. He also performed at music festivals and other venues until his death in 2018.\n\n==Biography==\n===Childhood and military service===\nHart was born to a [[sharecropping|sharecropper]] family in [[Loachapoka, Alabama]], United States,<ref name=\"AlamHOF\">[http://www.alamhof.org/freddiehart.html Alabama Music Hall of Fame Biography] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090304134031/http://www.alamhof.org/freddiehart.html |date=March 4, 2009 }}, Alamhof.org; retrieved September 18, 2008</ref> and spent his childhood in nearby [[Phenix City, Alabama]], along with his 11 siblings (Nadine, Bo, Junior, Olin, Marrell, Pearl, Lonnie, Sandra, Gail, J.P., Harold, and a child who died in infancy). He learned to play guitar at age 5 and quit school by age 12. At age 15, Hart lied about his age to join the [[United States Marine Corps|U.S. Marine Corps]] during [[World War II]], seeing combat action on [[Guam]] and [[Iwo Jima]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Following the war, Hart lived in California where he taught classes in self-defense at the Los Angeles Police Academy.<ref name=\"AlamHOF\" />\n\n===Early career===\nHart got an early career break when singer [[Carl Smith (country musician)|Carl Smith]] [[cover version|covered]] Hart's song \"[[Loose Talk (song)|Loose Talk]]\" in 1955. Other artists who recorded his songs included [[Patsy Cline]] (\"Lovin' In Vain\"), [[George Jones]] (\"My Tears are Overdue\") and [[Porter Wagoner]] (\"Skid Row Joe\").\n\nDuring the early 1950s, Hart and his family moved to California to further the growing country music scene there. In 1951, he joined [[Lefty Frizzell]]'s band for a year.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> It was through Frizzell that Hart got his first recording contract with [[Capitol Records]] in 1953.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> He released several singles including his version of \"Loose Talk\", but none of these were successful.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> In 1958, Hart signed with [[Columbia Records]] and scored his first chart hit with \"The Wall\" in 1959 which made the Top 20.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> His biggest hit for the label was the 1960 Top 20 hit \"The Key's In The Mailbox\".\n\nIn 1965, Hart signed with [[Kapp Records]] where he would score several Top 40 hits between 1965 and 1968. The biggest of these hits included \"Hank Williams' Guitar\" (1965), \"Born A Fool\" (1968) and \"Togetherness\" (1968).\n\n===Re-signing with Capitol Records and Easy Loving===\nIn 1969, Hart re-signed with Capitol Records and soon became a part of the [[Bakersfield sound]] by signing up with [[Buck Owens]]' songwriting and management company. In early 1970, he scored a Top 30 hit with \"The Whole World's Holdin' Hands\". Hart's song \"Togetherness\", a hit for him in 1968, became a Top 15 hit for Buck Owens and [[Susan Raye]] that summer. Hart would score several minor hits during the year.\n\nIn 1971, Hart released a song that he wrote called \"[[Easy Loving]]\" which was first recorded in the summer of 1969 for his album ''California Grapevine'', released in 1970.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Released in the summer of 1971, \"Easy Loving\" rapidly began climbing the charts; and by that September, it was No. 1 for three weeks on the country chart and reached No. 17 on the pop chart. It was also played on adult contemporary stations, earning a position on ''Billboard's'' Easy Listening survey. The song would ultimately win Hart numerous awards from both the [[Academy of Country Music]] and [[Country Music Association]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> The song sold over one million copies, and was awarded a [[music recording sales certification|gold record]] by the [[R.I.A.A.]] in November 1971.<ref name=\"The Book of Golden Discs\">{{cite book\n| first= Joseph\n| last= Murrells\n| year= 1978\n| title= The Book of Golden Discs\n| edition= 2nd\n| publisher= Barrie and Jenkins Ltd\n| location= London\n| page= [https://archive.org/details/bookofgoldendisc00murr/page/294 294]\n| isbn= 0-214-20512-6\n| url-access= registration\n| url= https://archive.org/details/bookofgoldendisc00murr/page/294\n}}</ref> The album of the same name also reportedly went gold. The song also earned Hart a [[Grammy Award]] nomination.\n\nFrom this success, Hart and his backup band, the Heartbeats, had a string of Top 5 hits with \"[[My Hang-Up Is You]]\" (six weeks at No. 1 in 1972), \"[[Bless Your Heart (song)|Bless Your Heart]]\" (No. 1 in 1972), \"[[Got the All Overs For You (All Over Me)]]\" (No. 1 in 1972), \"If You Can't Feel It (It Ain't There)\" (1973), \"[[Super Kind of Woman]]\" (No. 1 in 1973), \"[[Trip to Heaven]]\" (No. 1 in 1973), \"Hang In There Girl\" (1974), \"The Want-To's\" (1974), \"My Woman's Man\" (1975), \"The First Time\" (1975), \"I'd Like To Sleep Till I Get Over You\" (1975) and \"The Warm Side of You\" (1975).<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> He has been called by many fans as \"The Heart and Soul of Country Music\".{{Citation needed|date=May 2008}}\n\nWith the success of \"Easy Loving\" and other songs he wrote, plus a popular concert attraction on the road, Hart became independently wealthy and owned a songwriting company, a school for the blind, a trucking company, and a chain of [[martial arts]] studios\u2014his hobby was as a master of karate.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\n===Late 1970s\u20131980s===\nBy 1976, Hart continued to have major hits although now his streak of Top 10s were replaced by a streak of Top 20 and Top 30 hits. These included \"You Are The Song Inside Of Me\" (1976), \"That Look In Her Eyes\" (1976), \"Thank God She's Mine\" (1977), \"The Pleasure's Been All Mine\" (1977), \"Toe to Toe\" (1978), and \"Wasn't It Easy Baby\" (1979). His last Top 10 hit came with the hit \"Why Lovers Turn to Strangers\" in 1977, which peaked at No. 8. This song was written by east Idaho based composer Bobby Fender.\n\nIn 1980, Hart signed with [[Sunbird Records]], and immediately scored a Top 20 hit with \"Sure Thing\" that year. He followed this up with three Top 40 hits in 1981. This ended his days as a major country artist. In 1985 and 1987, he had a couple of minor hits on El Dorado and 5th Avenue Records, with his last hit being \"The Best Love I Never Had\" in 1987 peaking at No. 77.\n\n===Later years and death===\nIn 2001, Hart was inducted into the [[Alabama Music Hall of Fame]]<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.alamhof.org/freddiehart|title=Biography|website=Alabama Music Hall of Fame|access-date=August 7, 2021}}</ref> A few years later, Phenix City declared a major east\u2013west street Freddie Hart Parkway in his honor.\n\nHart released a handful of new albums on CD, showcasing his passion for gospel music, patriotism and the traditional country sound that originally made him famous. These albums prompted him to selectively tour and perform concerts around the world. Hart retained a large following in Europe and the U.S., performing at music festivals, universities, churches and industry events.\n\nHart continued to write and record gospel music during the 2000s. He received numerous awards and had several number one songs in the gospel field. In 2004 he was inducted into the Nashville Songwriter's Hall Of Fame. In 2017 he performed in Pigeon Forge Tennessee and received the Hall Of Fame award from the North American Country Music Associations International. His final performance was in March 2018 on the [[Ernest Tubb]] [[Midnite Jamboree]] as a special guest to [[David Frizzell]]. Hart sang a new song he had written and just recorded about Lefty Frizzell, titled simply \"Lefty\". In April 2018, Hart recorded his final album titled ''God Bless You''. The project, produced by David Frizzell, contains 11 newly written gospel songs and a remake of his signature song \"Easy Loving\". The album was released in late 2018.\n\nHart died as a result of pneumonia on October 27, 2018, in [[Burbank, California]].<ref name=\"Obit\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/8482008/freddie-hart-obituary-dead-at-91|title=Freddie Hart, Classic Country Singer and Songwriter, Dead at 91|website=Billboard|access-date=August 7, 2021}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Year\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Album\n! colspan=\"2\"| Chart Positions\n! \"I Don't Want to Lose You\"\n| align=\"center\"| 81\n|\n|-\n| 1987\n| \"Best Love I Never Had\"\n| align=\"center\"| 77\n|\n|}\n*<sup>A</sup>\"Easy Loving\" also peaked at No. 17 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Billboard Hot 100|Hot 100]], No. 31 on the Canadian ''[[RPM (magazine)|RPM]]'' Adult Contemporary Tracks chart and No. 21 on the ''RPM'' Top Singles chart.\n\n==The Heartbeats==\nFreddie Hart first used the name Heartbeats, a play on his last name, as his backing on a one-off 1967 album credited to Freddie Hart and the Heartbeats, but after his hit \"[[Easy Loving]]\" in 1971, ten studio albums were released between 1972 and 1977 credited to Freddie Hart and the Heartbeats. Various musicians performed in the Heartbeats over the years, including Bobby Wayne and Dennis Hromek, both of whom would go on to join [[The Strangers (American band)|the Strangers]]. During their heyday in the mid-1970s, the Heartbeats even released one studio album credited to just themselves in 1975.\n\n{{#tag:timeline|\nImageSize = width:1200 height:auto barincrement:25\nPlotArea = left:100 bottom:80 top:0 right:0\nAlignbars = justify\nDateFormat = mm/dd/yyyy\nPeriod = from:01/01/1967 till:12/31/1977\nTimeAxis = orientation:horizontal format:yyyy\n\nLegend = orientation:horizontal position:bottom\n\nColors =\n  id:gtr     value:blue      legend:Rhythm_Guitar_and_Front_Man\n  id:steel    value:green       legend:Steel_Guitar_and_Band_Leader\n  id:lead   value:orange legend:Lead_Guitar\n  id:organ    value:pink        legend:Guitorgan\n  id:bass     value:purple      legend:Bass\n  id:drums     value:yellow        legend:Drums\n\nScaleMajor = unit:year increment:2 start:1967\nScaleMinor = unit:year increment:1 start:1977\n\nBarData =\n   bar:Bobby    text:\"Bobby Wayne\"\n   bar:Dennis    text:\"Dennis Hromek\"\n   bar:Jimmy text:\"Jimmy Collins\"\n   bar:Dave   text:\"Dave Allen\"\n   bar:Buddy     text:\"Buddy Church\"\n   bar:Marc     text:\"Marc Chase\"\n   bar:Jim    text:\"Jim Morin\"\n   bar:JD    text:\"JD Walters\" \n   bar:Glen  text:\"Glen Brodeur\"\n   bar:Archie   text:\"Archie Michaud\"\n\nPlotData =\n   width:10\n   bar:Bobby   from:01/01/1967 till:01/01/1968 color:gtr\n   bar:Dave from:01/01/1967 till:01/01/1968 color:steel\n   bar:Dennis from:01/01/1967 till:01/01/1968 color:bass\n   bar:Jimmy from:01/01/1967 till:01/01/1968 color:drums\n   bar:Marc from:01/01/1972 till:12/31/1977 color:gtr\n   bar:JD from:01/01/1972 till:12/31/1977 color:steel\n   bar:Buddy from:01/01/1972 till:12/31/1977 color:lead\n   bar:Jim from:01/01/1972 till:12/31/1977 color:organ\n   bar:Glen from:01/01/1972 till:12/31/1977 color:bass\n   bar:Archie   from:01/01/1972 till:12/31/1977 color:drums\n    \n}}\n\n==Awards and nominations==\n{|class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! Gatlin"}],"pages":{"1683504":{"pageid":1683504,"ns":0,"title":"Larry Gatlin","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2023}}\n{{Short description|American country and gospel singer-songwriter (born 1948)}}\n{{BLP sources|date=May 2008}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Larry Gatlin\n| image               = Larry Gatlin.JPG\n| image_size          = \n| caption             = Gatlin in 2009\n| background          = person\n| birth_name          = Larry Wayne Gatlin\n| birth_date          = {{Birth date and age|1948|5|2}}\n| birth_place         = [[Seminole, Texas]], U.S.\n| origin              = <!-- only if different than birth_place -->\n| genre               = {{Hlist | [[Country music|Country]] | [[Gospel music|gospel]]}}\n| occupation          = Singer-songwriter\n| years_active        = 1973\u2013present\n| label               = {{Hlist | [[Monument Records|Monument]] | [[Columbia Records|Columbia]] | [[Universal Records (1988 record label)|Universal]] | [[Capitol Records|Capitol]] | [[Curb Records|Curb]]}}\n| associated_acts     = [[Dottie West]], [[Kris Kristofferson]], [[Janie Fricke]], [[Kenny Rogers]]<!-- associated_acts is deprecated -->\n| past_member_of      = [[The Imperials]]\n| current_member_of   = The Gatlin Brothers\n| website             = {{url|www.gatlinbrothers.com/}}\n}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = The Gatlin Brothers\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| genre               = {{Hlist | [[Country music|Country]] | [[Gospel music|gospel]]}}\n| years_active        = 1973\u2013present\n| label               = {{Hlist | [[Monument Records|Monument]] | [[Columbia Records|Columbia]] | Universal<!--different Universal label owned by Jimmy Bowen, merged with Capitol in '89--> | [[Capitol Records|Capitol]] | [[Curb Records|Curb]]}}\n| current_members     = {{hlist|Larry Gatlin|Rudy Gatlin|Steve Gatlin}}\n}}\n\n'''Larry Wayne Gatlin''' (born May 2, 1948)<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=153}}</ref> is an American [[country music|country]] and [[Southern gospel]] singer-songwriter. As part of [[the Gatlin Brothers]] trio that included his younger brothers Steve and Rudy, he achieved considerable success within the country music genre, performing on 33 top 40 country singles, a total inclusive of his recordings as a solo artist and with the group.\n\nGatlin is known for his tenor voice and for the country songs that he recorded in the 1970s and 1980s. Some of Gatlin's greatest hits include \"[[Broken Lady]]\", \"[[All the Gold in California]]\", \"[[Houston (Means I'm One Day Closer to You)]]\", \"She Used to Be Somebody's Baby\" and \"Night Time Magic\". During this time, country music trended toward slick pop-music arrangements in a style that came to be known as [[Countrypolitan]]. Gatlin and the Gatlin Brothers came to prominence and enjoyed their greatest success during this period with hit singles that showcased the brothers' rich gospel-inflected harmonies and Larry's poetic lyrics.\n\n== Early life ==\nGatlin was born in [[Seminole, Texas|Seminole]] in [[Gaines County, Texas]], United States,<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> next to the [[New Mexico]] border. His father was an oilfield worker, and the family lived in several locations while he was a youth, including [[Abilene, Texas|Abilene]] and [[Odessa, Texas|Odessa]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> He was reared listening to country and Southern gospel music. He has performed with his brothers Steve and Rudy since childhood. When they were younger, they often sang at their local church along with their sister [[LaDonna Gatlin|LaDonna]]<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> and occasionally performed on local radio and television shows. They also recorded a gospel music album for the Sword and Shield label and topped [[Roy Orbison]] in a local talent contest.{{citation needed|date=September 2014}}\n\nGatlin was a quarterback at [[Odessa High School (Texas)|Odessa High School]]. After graduation in 1966, he was eligible to serve in the military during the [[Vietnam War]],<ref>{{cite web\n| url        = http://thelittleredblog.typepad.com/blog/2014/09/president-gatlin-declares-world-war-iii.html\n| title      = President Gatlin Declares World War III\n| author       = Jack Shifflett\n| date       = September 4, 2014\n| access-date = September 7, 2014\n}}</ref> but he chose to attend the [[University of Houston]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> As a [[wide receiver]] on the [[Houston Cougars football|football team]], he caught a [[touchdown]] pass in a 1968 game in which his team scored 100 points.<ref>{{cite web\n| url        = http://bill37mccurdy.wordpress.com/tag/houston-100-tulsa-6-1968/\n| title      = 1968: About That Houston 100-Points Game\n| work       = The Pecan Park Eagle\n| date       = September 15, 2013\n| access-date = September 7, 2014\n}}</ref>\n\nHe later auditioned for and joined the gospel music group [[the Imperials]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.sghistory.com/index.php?n=I.Imperials|title=Southern Gospel History &#124; I / Imperials|website=Sghistory.com}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.pbs.org/klru/austin/artists/program290.html|title=PBS \u2013 Austin City Limits|website=[[PBS]] |date=November 11, 2001|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20011111093015/http://www.pbs.org/klru/austin/artists/program290.html|access-date=2021-08-07|archive-date=2001-11-11}}</ref> The Imperials went on to perform in [[Las Vegas, Nevada|Las Vegas]] in January 1971 at ''[[Jimmy Dean|Jimmy Dean's Las Vegas Revue]]''. While walking through the showroom, Gatlin caught country singer [[Dottie West]]'s attention, who thought that he resembled [[Mickey Newbury]].{{citation needed|date=March 2022}} West was impressed with Gatlin's songwriting skills, and she recorded two of his compositions, \"You're the Other Half of Me\" and \"Once You Were Mine\".<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\" /> West also passed one of Gatlin's [[demo (music)|demo tapes]] around [[Nashville, Tennessee]], and arranged for him to relocate there by purchasing a plane ticket for him.{{citation needed|date=March 2022}} West recorded other compositions by Gatlin that would later become hits for him, including \"Broken Lady\", which appeared on West's 1978 album ''[[Dottie (album)|Dottie]]''.\n\n=== As a solo artist ===\nWith West's help, Gatlin found work in Nashville as a [[Backing vocalist|background singer]] for [[Kris Kristofferson]]. In 1973, Gatlin landed a solo recording contract with [[Monument Records]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\nIn December 1973, Gatlin released his first album, ''The Pilgrim''.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Two singles were released from the album: \"Sweet Becky Walker\" and \"Bitter They Are, Harder They Fall\", although both failed to chart.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> The latter song was recorded by [[Elvis Presley]] in 1976 (who had also recorded Gatlin's \"[[Help Me (Larry Gatlin song)|Help Me]]\" in 1973).<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> 1974 saw the release of a new album, ''Rain/Rainbow'', and the song \"Delta Dirt\". The album and single proved more successful; \"Delta Dirt\" was a top-20 country hit, peaking at number 14. The song was also Gatlin's only entry into the pop charts, when it reached number 84. In 1975, Gatlin had his first major hit with his composition \"Broken Lady\", which reached number five on the [[Hot Country Songs]] chart in 1976<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> and won him a [[Grammy Award]] for [[Best Country Song]].<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> A new album, ''High Time'', was released in 1976.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Gatlin is also credited on guitar on [[Willie Nelson]]'s 1976 album ''[[The Troublemaker (album)|The Troublemaker]]''.{{citation needed|date=August 2014}}\n\nBrothers Steve and Rudy made their first appearance on Larry's 1976 album ''Larry Gatlin with Family & Friends''. They were featured on some of Gatlin's other hits during the late 1970s, notably \"I Don't Wanna Cry\", \"Love Is Just a Game\" and \"Statues Without Hearts\".<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> In 1978, Gatlin scored his first number-one hit with \"[[I Just Wish You Were Someone I Love]]\".<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> In 1978, he released his last solo album, ''Oh Brother'', which featured the top-10 hits \"I've Done Enough Dyin' Today\" and \"[[Night Time Magic]]\". The latter song reached the [[Adult Contemporary (chart)|''Billboard'' Easy Listening]] chart. Both songs spotlighted Gatlin's soaring falsetto that became a trademark of his vocal style.\n\nIn 1985, Gatlin purchased shares in the [[Nashville Sounds]], a [[Minor League Baseball]] team of the [[Triple-A (baseball)|Triple-A]] [[American Association (20th century)|American Association]].<ref>{{citation|first=Larry|last=Woody|title=Schmittou: A Grand Slam in Baseball, Business, And Life|publisher=Eggmann Publishing Company|location=Nashville|year=1996|isbn=1886371334|pages=64\u201365}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |date=1985 |title=Sounds Owners |work=The Nashville Sounds 1985 Official Souvenir Program |publisher=Nashville Sounds |page=6}}</ref>\n\n=== With the Gatlin Brothers ===\n[[File:Gatlin Brothers Nashville Sounds 1985.jpg|thumb|upright=1.3|left|The Gatlin Brothers in the uniforms of the [[Nashville Sounds]] in 1985 (from left to right: Larry, Steve and Rudy)]]\nIn 1979, when Gatlin signed with [[Columbia Records]], he decided to officially have his brothers billed as Larry Gatlin & the Gatlin Brothers. In October, they released the album ''Straight Ahead''. It spawned the single \"[[All the Gold in California]]\", which became their greatest hit together, reaching number one on the [[Hot Country Songs]] list. This was Gatlin's second number-one hit, and he was named Top Male Vocalist of the Year by the [[Academy of Country Music]]. On June 6, 1980, ''Straight Ahead'' was certified gold.\n\nThe group's next big hit came in early 1980 with \"Take Me to Your Lovin' Place\", which peaked at number five in 1981. They next released \"What Are We Doin' Lonesome\", which peaked at number four later in the year. They continued with top-10 and top-20 hits such as \"In Like with Each Other\" (1982), \"She Used to Sing on Sunday\" (1982), \"Sure Feels Like Love\" (1982), \"Almost Called Her Baby by Mistake\" (1983) and \"Denver\" (1984). In 1983, the group released their third and last number-one hit, \"Houston (Means I'm One Day Closer to You)\". On January 19, 1985, the Gatlin Brothers sang \"All the Gold in California\" at the nationally televised second inauguration gala for [[Ronald Reagan]]. Though the group never achieved another number-one hit, they came close with \"She Used to Be Somebody's Baby\" (1986, number two), \"Talkin' to the Moon\" (1987, number four) and \"Love of a Lifetime\" (1988, number four).\n\nThe Gatlin Brothers were also one of the first country groups to appear in music videos, such as [[1984 in country music|1984's]] \"[[The Lady Takes the Cowboy Everytime]]\"{{Sic}}. In 1985, Gatlin wrote the song \"Indian Summer\" with [[Barry Gibb]], which he recorded as a duet with [[Roy Orbison]]. In 1989, the Gatlin Brothers sang \"[[The Star-Spangled Banner]]\" before Game 3 of the [[1989 World Series]] at [[Candlestick Park]] in San Francisco just before the [[1989 Loma Prieta earthquake|Loma Prieta earthquake]] occurred. They also sang the national anthem at Game 5 of the [[1985 World Series]] and Game 6 of the [[2005 NBA Finals]].{{citation needed|date=July 2015}}\n\n=== Later work ===\nGatlin's chart success declined greatly when a new breed of [[neotraditional country]] singers entered Nashville around 1986. New stars such as [[Dwight Yoakam]] and [[Randy Travis]] pushed Gatlin and other Countrypolitan vocalists out of the top 10. Gatlin recorded a duet in 1987 with country-pop singer [[Janie Fricke]],<ref>''The Billboard Book Of Top Country Hits'', Joel Whitburn, {{ISBN|0-8230-8291-1}}, 2006</ref> but the song reached only number 21. He briefly signed with [[Universal Records (1988)|Universal Records]] in 1989, where he recorded his last singles. His last charting single was released in 1989, titled \"Number One Heartache Place\". Gatlin underwent surgery on his vocal cords in 1991. In concert, he had begun to struggle with the high falsetto notes that were featured prominently in many of his songs. After recovery, Gatlin worked briefly with an opera coach to rebuild his voice, and his vocals took a powerful operatic style.{{citation needed|date=March 2022}}\n\n[[File:Larry Gatlin playing cards in Croatia.JPEG|thumb|Gatlin (left) playing cards with [[Seabee (US Navy)|Seabee]]s in [[Croatia]] after a performance in 1995]]\nAfter more than a decade of singing together, in December 1992, the Gatlin Brothers embarked on a farewell tour before retiring to their own theater in [[Myrtle Beach, South Carolina]]. Gatlin starred in the [[Broadway theatre|Broadway]] production of ''The Will Rogers Follies''. In 1994, Gatlin and his brothers opened a 2,000-seat theater in Myrtle Beach. In 1995, he played himself in the television movie about [[Dottie West]]'s life, ''Big Dreams & Broken Hearts: The Dottie West Story''. West had been killed four years earlier in an automobile accident.\n\nAlong with [[celebrity biographer]] Jeff Lenburg, Gatlin wrote a memoir titled ''All the Gold in California'' that was published in 1998. In 1999, Gatlin toured and entertained troops of the [[1st Cavalry Division (United States)|1st Cavalry Division]] in [[Bosnia and Herzegovina|Bosnia]].{{citation needed|date=March 2022}}\n\nSince 2010, Gatlin has contributed to [[Fox News Channel]] and [[Fox Business Network]] as a political and social commentator. In 2010, Gatlin acted as substitute host for [[Don Imus]] on ''[[Imus in the Morning]]''<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2010/06/01/larry-gatlin-don-imus/|title=Larry Gatlin to Sit In for Vacationing Don Imus|website=Theboot.com|date=June 2010 }}</ref> and on ''Fox Across America with Spencer Hughes'' on March 16, 2011. He also hosts radio shows for [[WSM (AM)|WSM]], including a weekly gospel program, and the ''[[Grand Ole Opry]]'' spinoff ''Opry Country Classics''.{{citation needed|date=March 2022}}\n\nIn 2023 Larry, Steve, and Rudy [[The Gatlin Brothers]] have released two new singles; \"Fair Winds\" and \"Amazing' (What Just The Right 3 Minutes Can Do)\"\n\n== Discography ==\n{{Main|Larry Gatlin discography}}\n\n== References ==\n{{Reflist|30em}}\n\n==Sources==\n* Wood, Gerry. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Ira_Louvin","to":"Ira Louvin"}],"pages":{"4255555":{"pageid":4255555,"ns":0,"title":"Ira Louvin","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer-songwriter (1924\u20131965)}}\n\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2020}}\n{{More citations needed|date=July 2007}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Ira Louvin\n| image                 = \n| caption            =\n| image_size            =\n| background          = solo_singer \n| birth_name          = Ira Lonnie Loudermilk\n| alias               = \n| birth_date                = {{birth date|1924|4|21|mf=y}}\n| death_date                =  {{death date and age|1965|6|20|1924|4|21}}  \n|death_place =[[Williamsburg, Missouri]], U.S.\n| origin              = [[Section, Alabama]], U.S.\n| instrument          = [[Mandolin]]\n| genre               = [[Country music|Country]], [[Gospel music|gospel]]\n| occupation          = Singer, songwriter\n| years_active        = 1940\u20131965\n| label               = [[MGM]], [[Capitol Records|Capitol]]\n| associated_acts     = [[The Louvin Brothers]]\n}}\n'''Ira Lonnie Loudermilk''' (April 21, 1924 \u2013 June 20, 1965), known professionally as '''Ira Louvin''', was an American [[country music]] singer, [[mandolin]]ist and songwriter. He was a cousin of songwriter [[John D. Loudermilk]].\n\n==Biography==\nIra Louvin was born in [[Section, Alabama]], and played together with his brother, [[Charlie Louvin|Charlie]], in the [[close harmony]] tradition as [[the Louvin Brothers]]. They were heavily influenced by [[the Delmore Brothers]] and Monroe Brothers. Ira played mandolin with [[Charlie Monroe]], guitar player of the Monroe Brothers in the early 1940s. The Louvin Brothers' songs were heavily influenced by their Baptist faith and warned against sin.\n\nIra was notorious for his drinking and short temper. He married four times, his third wife having shot him multiple times in the chest and hand after he allegedly beat her.<ref>{{cite news|title='Opry' Singer Star Shot; Wife Jailed|newspaper=The Miami Herald|date=February 21, 1963|url=https://www.newspapers.com/clip/4881654/ira-louvin-shooting-1963/|archive-url=https://archive.today/20220216142651/https://www.newspapers.com/clip/4881654/ira-louvin-shooting-1963/|url-status=dead|archive-date=2022-02-16|access-date=February 16, 2022}}</ref> He died on June 20, 1965, when a drunken driver struck his car in [[Williamsburg, Missouri]].<ref>{{cite news|last=Strauss|first=Neil|title=The Pop Life|newspaper=The New York Times|date=November 28, 1996|url=https://www.nytimes.com/1996/11/28/arts/the-pop-life-500887.html?pagewanted=1|access-date=January 22, 2010}}</ref> At the time, a warrant for Louvin's arrest had been issued on a DUI charge.\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n*{{Official This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Jordanaires","to":"The Jordanaires"}],"pages":{"1775193":{"pageid":1775193,"ns":0,"title":"The Jordanaires","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American vocal group; back-up singers for Elvis Presley and other artists}}\n{{Use American English|date=April 2018}}\n{{More citations needed|date= January 2018}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name             = The Jordanaires\n| background       = group_or_band\n| image            = File:Elvis Presley and the Jordanaires 1957.jpg\n| caption          = The Jordanaires with [[Elvis Presley]], 1957\n| origin           = [[Springfield, Missouri]], United States\n| genre            = [[Gospel music|Gospel]], [[Country music|country]], [[rock and roll]], [[Folk music|folk]]\n| years_active     = {{Start date|1948}}\u2013{{End date|2013}}<ref name=\"Cooper\">{{cite web|url=http://blogs.tennessean.com/tunein/2013/03/27/gordon-stoker-leader-of-elvis-presleys-jordanaires-dies-bringing-legendary-group-to-end/|title=Jordanaires leader Gordon Stoker dies|last=Cooper|first=Peter|work=[[The Tennessean]]|date=March 27, 2013|access-date=June 2, 2013}}</ref>\n| label            = \n| associated_acts  = [[Foggy River Boys]], [[Patsy Cline]], [[Elvis Presley]], [[Eddy Arnold]], [[Jim Reeves]], [[Ricky Nelson]], [[Ringo Starr]], [[Ween]], [[Johnny Cash]], [[Dolly Parton]]\n| website          = {{URL|jordanaires.net}}\n| past_members     = {{ubl|[[Ray Walker (singer)|Ray Walker]]|Curtis Young|Gordon Stoker|Bill Matthews|Bob Hubbard|Warren (Monty) Matthews|Culley Holt|Hoyt Hawkins|[[Neal Matthews Jr.]]|Don Bruce|Hugh Jarrett|Duane West|Louis Nunley}}\n}}\n'''The Jordanaires''' were an [[Americans|American]] vocal quartet that formed as a [[Gospel music|gospel]] group in 1948. Over the years, they recorded both sacred and secular music for recording companies such as [[Capitol Records]], [[RCA Victor]], [[Columbia Records]], [[Decca Records]], [[Vocalion Records]], Stop Records, and many other smaller independent labels.{{Citation needed|date=September 2020}}\n\nIn the mid-1950s, with a lineup of Gordon Stoker (first tenor), Neal Matthews (second tenor and lead vocals), Hoyt Hawkins (baritone and lead vocals), and Hugh Jarrett (bass vocals), they also began lending their vocal talents to other artists as background singers in recording sessions.  They are widely known for having provided background vocals for [[Elvis Presley]] in live appearances, recordings, and feature films from 1956 to 1970. Jarrett was replaced by then-teacher [[Ray Walker (singer)|Ray Walker]] in 1958. The group worked in the recording studio, on stage, and on television with many [[Country music|country]], [[Gospel music|gospel]], and [[Rock music|rock and roll]] artists.\n\nThey also provided background vocals using the names the Gordonaires (a play on the name of the group's first tenor Gordon Stoker), the Merry Melody Singers, and the Almanac Singers, sometimes using different personnel.\n\n==Group history==\n===Early years===\n\nThe group was formed by brothers Monty and Bill Matthews, both of whom were evangelists, in the late 1940s.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\">{{cite web |last1=Rumble |first1=John |title=Jordanaires |url=https://www.countrymusichalloffame.org/hall-of-fame/jordanaires |website=Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum |publisher=Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum |access-date=August 22, 2024}}</ref>  The original lineup included Bill Matthews, Monty Matthews, Bob Hubbard (baritone), Culley Holt (bass vocals), soon joined by pianist Bob Money.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>  By 1949, the group members had moved from [[Springfield, Missouri]] to [[Nashville, Tennessee]].<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>  <!-- edit here: In 1948, Monty and Bill Matthews left. Hawkins switched to baritone, and new lead [[Neal Matthews]] was recruited. Don Bruce came in as a new first tenor, but he was drafted the next year. The group narrowed to a quartet, with Gordon Stoker taking over as first tenor. -->  \n\nThey became members of the [[Grand Ole Opry]] in 1949,<ref>{{cite web| title = Opry Timeline \u2013 1940s| url = http://www.opry.com/about/Timeline_1940.html| website = Opry.com| access-date = July 6, 2012| archive-date = March 17, 2017| archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20170317065341/http://www.opry.com/about/Timeline_1940.html| url-status = dead}}</ref><ref name=\"Rovi\">{{cite web | title = The Jordanaires | url = http://www.allmusic.com/artist/the-jordanaires-mn0000087113 | publisher = [[AllMusic]] | date = 2012 | access-date = July 6, 2012}}</ref> where they frequently provided harmony and backing vocals for Opry \"headliner\" [[Red Foley]].<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>  In the early 1950s, the group featured many lineup changes. Pianist Bob Money was replaced by Gordon Stoker, and founding members Bill and Monty Matthews left the group and moved back to Missouri.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>  Stoker began singing with the group, taking on lead vocal and tenor roles, and new members [[Neal Matthews, Jr.]] (second tenor, and unrelated to Bill and Monty Matthews), Hoyt Hawkins (baritone), and Hugh Jarrett (bass vocals) joined in the early-to-mid-1950s.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nSister Rosetta Tharpe toured with the vocal group the Jordanaires in the late forties and early fifties, one of the first multiracial gospel pairings.\n\nThey recorded for [[Capitol Records]] in the early 1950s, and began providing vocal accompaniment behind solo singers in Nashville, Tennessee.<ref name=\"Rovi\" /><ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nThe quartet became well known in the Southern gospel genre, and what made them stand out from other quartets of that time was how they would bring [[spirituals]] (such as \"Dry Bones\") to a predominantly white audience. While continuing to turn out gospel albums of their own, the group became better known for the signature background harmonies they provided on dozens of secular records.<ref name=CMT>{{cite web|title=Jordanaires Biography|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/jordanaires/bio.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20040731212016/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/jordanaires/bio.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=July 31, 2004|website=Cmt.com|access-date=11 May 2011}}</ref><ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nIn the late 1950s, member Neal Matthews, Jr. created the [[Nashville Number System]] for the Jordanaires (and the [[Nashville A-Team]]) to use to make recording easier and simplify any potential key changes during recording.<ref>{{Cite web|title=The Nashville Number System |author= Chas Williams|url=https://nashvillenumbersystem.com/|access-date=January 21, 2023|website=nashvillenumbersystem.com}}</ref><ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\n===Elvis Presley===\n\nAccording to the Jordanaires' website, in 1955, they first met musician Elvis Presley, a fan of the group, backstage after a concert in Memphis, Tennessee with Eddy Arnold; at the time, Presley was signed to the Memphis-based label Sun Records.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>  During this meeting, Presley told the group that he would like them to sing backup for him if he ever was signed to a major record label.  Stoker later stated that the group \"[wished] Elvis well, 'But we never expected to hear from him again,' ... 'People were always coming up and saying that. We're still told that.'\"<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>\n\nAfter Elvis' contract was sold to [[RCA Records|RCA Victor Records]], he and his band [[the Blue Moon Boys]] (lead guitarist [[Scotty Moore]], [[double bass]]ist [[Bill Black]], and drummer [[D. J. Fontana]]) had their first RCA sessions in January 1956.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>  His co-producer, guitarist [[Chet Atkins]], recruited Stoker to sing backup for \"a 'new-probably-wouldn't-be-around-long kid, named Elvis Presley'\".<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>    Instead of recruiting all of the Jordanaires, as Presley had wanted, Chet Atkins hired Ben and Brock Speer of the vocal group the Speer Family, who had also recently signed to RCA, to sing with Stoker.  Elvis, his band, Stoker, and Ben and Brock Speer, recorded  \"I Was The One\" (the B-side of \"[[Heartbreak Hotel]]\") in January and \"[[I Want You, I Need You, I Love You]]\" in April.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>  After the April session, Presley asked Stoker if the full group could join him in the studio for the next sessions.  Stoker arranged this, and the full group began working with Presley shortly afterwards.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>  They continued recording (and touring) with Presley regularly until 1968, and sporadically rejoined him for some sessions in 1970 and 1971.\n\n===Patsy Cline===\nThe group appeared on all of [[Patsy Cline]]'s [[Decca Records|Decca]] sessions from her first in November 1960 to her last in February 1963, during which time they backed her on songs such as:\n{{Div col|colwidth=22em}}\n*\"[[A Poor Man's Roses (Or a Rich Man's Gold)]]\"\n*\"[[Always (Irving Berlin song)|Always]]\"\n*\"[[Blue Moon of Kentucky]]\"\n*\"[[Crazy (Willie Nelson song)|Crazy]]\"\n*\"[[Crazy Arms]]\"\n*\"[[Faded Love]]\"\n*\"[[Foolin' Around (Buck Owens song)|Foolin' Around]]\"\n*\"[[Half as Much]]\"\n*\"[[Have You Ever Been Lonely?|Have You Ever Been Lonely (Have You Ever Been Blue)?]]\"\n*\"[[Heartaches (song)|Heartaches]]\"\n*\"[[I Can't Help It (If I'm Still in Love with You)]]\"\n*\"[[I Fall to Pieces]]\"\n*\"[[Leavin' on Your Mind]]\"\n*\"[[Love Letters in the Sand]]\"\n*\"[[San Antonio Rose]]\"\n*\"[[Seven Lonely Days]]\"\n*\"[[She's Got You]]\"\n*\"[[Someday (You'll Want Me to Want You)]]\"\n*\"[[South of the Border (Down Mexico Way)]]\"\n*\"[[Sweet Dreams (Don Gibson song)|Sweet Dreams]]\"\n*\"[[That's My Desire]]\"\n*\"[[The Wayward Wind]]\"\n*\"[[True Love (Cole Porter song)|True Love]]\"\n*\"[[Walkin' After Midnight]]\" (1961 recording)\n*\"[[You Belong to Me (1952 song)|You Belong to Me]]\"\n*\"[[You Made Me Love You (I Didn't Want to Do It)]]\"\n*\"[[Your Cheatin' Heart]]\"\n<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.patsified.com/decca.html|title=Patsy Cline's Recording Sessions - The Decca Years|first=William L.|last=Cox|website=Patsified.com|access-date=7 September 2018}}</ref>\n{{div col end}}\n\n===After Elvis and Cline===\n\nAccording to the Jordanaires' official website, in 1976 and 1979, [[The Recording Academy|the National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences]] gave the group the \"Superpickers\" award \"for having sung on more Top 10 discs than any other vocal group in history.\"<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>  \n\nThe group's lineup changed again in 1982, when Hoyt Hawkins died. His replacement was Duane West,<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref> formerly of [[Sonny James]]' backup group, the Southern Gentlemen, who had filled in for Hawkins on numerous occasions in the 1970s when Hawkins had been ill.\n\nIn 1984, they received the \"'CMA Masters Award' for their lifetime contribution of music\" from the Country Music Association.<ref>{{cite web |title=The Jordanaires Biography |url=http://www.jordanaires.net/about/us.htm |website=The Jordanaires |access-date=September 8, 2024}}</ref>\n\nIn 1990, the group provided backing vocals for Presley's former Sun Records labelmate [[Johnny Cash]] on his [[Mercury Records]] album ''[[Boom Chicka Boom]]''. The group also recorded with the Swedish group [[Vikingarna (band)|Vikingarna]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.aftonbladet.se/nojesbladet/musik/article10427694.ab|title=Vikingarna tar farv\u00e4l av fansen|website=Aftonbladet.se|language=sv|author=Linda Hjert\u00e9n|date=22 January 2004|access-date=14 December 2016}}</ref>\n\n===Later years and deaths===\n\nAccording to John Rumble and the Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum, in 2000, West left the group \"due to illness\".<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>  He was replaced by Louis Nunley.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>  That same year, longtime member Neal Matthews, Jr. died, and he was replaced by Curtis Young.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nIn 2001, the Jordanaires were inducted into both the Country Music Hall of Fame and the Gospel Music Hall of Fame.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nHugh Jarrett died at 78 on May 31, 2008, from injuries sustained in an auto accident in March.<ref name=\"Hugh Jarrett\">{{cite web|title=Hugh Jarrett|url=http://www.jordanaires.net/History/HughJarrett.htm|website=Jordanaires.net|access-date=March 28, 2013}}</ref><ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nGordon Stoker died at 88 at his [[Brentwood, Tennessee]], home on March 27, 2013, after a long illness. His son Alan confirmed that The Jordanaires were formally dissolved, per his father's wishes.<ref name=\"Cooper\"></ref><ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\nUnreleased recordings featuring the Jordanaires continue to be released. In 2023, Dolly Parton's [[Rockstar (Dolly Parton album)|''Rockstar'']]<ref>{{cite web|url=https://consequence.net/2023/05/dolly-parton-rockstar-tracklist-release/|title=The Tracklist for Dolly Parton's Rock Album is a Sight to Behold|last=Young|first=Alex|work=[[Consequence of Sound]]|date=May 9, 2023|access-date=October 19, 2023}}</ref> album was released, which features a previously recorded version of \"I Dreamed About Elvis\" featuring the quartet. Parton performed this song in concert as early as 2007.\n\nSurviving members include longtime member Ray Walker and later addition Curtis Young.<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\n==Members==\n{{Unreferenced section|date= March 2022}}\n\nPartial credits from the [[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum]].<ref name=\"Jordanaires CMHOF 1\"></ref>\n\n===Classic While released in 2023, the song was recorded at some point prior to 2013, when the group disbanded after Gordon Stoker's death.\n\n==See also==\n* [[The Nashville This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Penny_DeHaven","to":"Penny DeHaven"}],"pages":{"11471562":{"pageid":11471562,"ns":0,"title":"Penny DeHaven","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer-songwriter (1948\u20132014)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2020}}\n{{More citations needed|date=February 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Penny DeHaven\n| image           =\n| caption         =\n| image_size      =\n| background      = solo_singer\n| birth_name      = Charlotte DeHaven\n| alias           = Penny Starr\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date|1948|05|17}}\n| birth_place     = [[Winchester, Virginia]], U.S.\n| origin          = \n| death_date      = {{death date and age|2014|02|23|1948|05|17}}\n| instrument      =\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]], [[gospel music|gospel]]\n| occupation      = Singer\n| years_active    = 1967\u20132014\n| label           = [[United Artists]], Mainstreet, Elektra, Imperial\n| past_member_of = Del Reeves\n| website         =\n}}\n\n'''Charlotte''' \"'''Penny'''\" '''DeHaven''' (May 17, 1948<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=114}}</ref> \u2013 February 23, 2014)<ref name=musicrow/> was an American country and gospel music singer. At the beginning of her career, she recorded as '''Penny Starr'''.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\nShe was born in [[Winchester, Virginia]], United States,<ref name=\"CMT\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/dehaven_penny/bio.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20050216121337/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/dehaven_penny/bio.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=February 16, 2005|title=Penny DeHaven biography|last=Bush|first=John|publisher=Country Music Television|accessdate=March 17, 2010}}</ref> she is best known for her country hit singles in the late 1960s and early 1970s. Her biggest hit was \"Land Mark Tavern\", a duet with [[Del Reeves]] in 1970.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/>\n\nDeHaven's other singles included country remakes of such pop hits as [[Billy Joe Royal]]'s \"[[Down in the Boondocks (song)|Down in the Boondocks]]\" (1969), [[The Beatles]]' \"[[I Feel Fine]]\" (1970), [[The Everly Brothers]]' \"[[Crying in the Rain]]\" (with Reeves, 1972), and [[Marvin Gaye]]'s \"[[I'll Be Doggone]]\" (1974).<ref name=musicrow/>\n\nHer albums included 1972's ''Penny DeHaven'' and 2011's gospel collection ''A Penny Saved''.<ref name=musicrow/>\n\nAs an actress, she made two guest appearances on the CBS-TV/syndicated TV show ''[[Hee Haw]]'' in 1972\u201373.  She also appeared in the movies ''Traveling Light,'' ''Country Music Story,''<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> the 1973 horror movie ''Valley of Blood'', and the 1974 TV series ''[[Funny Farm (TV series)|Funny Farm]]''.\n\nDeHaven died from cancer on February 23, 2014, at the age of 65.<ref name=musicrow>{{cite news|last=Oermann|first=Robert K.|title=[Updated] Lifenotes: Penny DeHaven Passes|url=http://www.musicrow.com/2014/02/penny-dehaven-passes/|accessdate=February 25, 2014|newspaper=[[MusicRow]]|date=February 25, 2014}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"William_Lee_Golden","to":"William Lee Golden"}],"pages":{"9611501":{"pageid":9611501,"ns":0,"title":"William Lee Golden","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer (born 1939)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2023}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = William Lee Golden\n| image               = William Lee Golden by Gage Skidmore.jpg\n| caption             = Golden in 2013\n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = William Lee Golden\n| birth_date          = {{birth date and age|1939|1|12}}\n| origin              = [[Brewton, Alabama]], U.S.\n| instrument          = Vocals (baritone)\n| genre               = [[Country music|Country]], [[Gospel music|gospel]]\n| occupation          = Singer, painter, wizard\n| years_active        = 1965\u2013present\n| label               = [[MCA Records|MCA]], [[Mercury Records|Mercury]]\n| current_member_of = [[The Oak Ridge Boys]]\n| website             = {{url|www.williamleegolden.com}}\n}}\n'''William Lee Golden''' (born January 12, 1939)<ref>{{Cite book |last1=McCall |first1=Michael |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=XsiL49XFbnkC&dq=william+lee+golden+1939&pg=PT1575 |title=The Encyclopedia of Country Music |last2=Rumble |first2=John |last3=Kingsbury |first3=Paul |date=2004-12-16 |publisher=Oxford University Press |isbn=978-0-19-984044-1 |language=en}}</ref> is an American [[country music]] singer. Between 1965 and 1987, and again since December 1995, he has been the baritone singer in the country vocal group [[The Oak Ridge Boys]].\n\nGolden was inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum|Country Music Hall of Fame]] in 2015 as a member of the Oak Ridge Boys.\n\n==Career==\nGolden joined The Oak Ridge Boys (then a [[Southern gospel music]] group) in 1965. Golden is widely known for his waist-length beard and hair, and has become one of the most recognizable faces in the entertainment industry. Golden was voted out of The Oak Ridge Boys in 1987, as the other three members wanted to change the band's image.<ref name=\"news\"/> He was replaced by [[Steve Sanders (musician)|Steve Sanders]], but stayed with [[MCA Records]] as a solo artist to record an album titled ''American Vagabond'', which included two chart singles.<ref name=\"whitburn\">{{cite book|last=Whitburn|first=Joel|title=Hot Country Songs 1944 to 2008|publisher=Record Research, Inc|date=2008|page=164|isbn=978-0-89820-177-2}}</ref> In 1990, he moved to [[Mercury Records]] and released \"Louisiana Red Dirt Highway\".<ref name=\"news\">{{cite news|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1955&dat=19940812&id=a1UxAAAAIBAJ&sjid=SaIFAAAAIBAJ&pg=3648,5326579|title=When it comes to country music, he's Golden|last=Pe\u00f1a|first=Susan L.|date=12 August 1994|work=Reading Eagle|access-date=20 September 2011}}</ref>\n\nSanders left the group in 1995 and Golden returned on New Year's Eve of the same year.<ref>Whitburn, p. 303</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nHas been married four times.<ref name=people>{{cite journal |last1=McCall |first1=Cheryl |title=After Months on the Warpath, the Battling Oak Ridge Boys Pass the Peace Pipe |journal=People |date=April 25, 1983 |volume=19 |issue=16 |url=https://people.com/archive/after-months-on-the-warpath-the-battling-oak-ridge-boys-pass-the-peace-pipe-vol-19-no-16/ |access-date=10 November 2018}}</ref>\nGolden was married to Frogene Normand from 1957 to 1975. He married Luetta Callaway in 1984 and they divorced in 1987. He was married to Brenda Kaye Hall from 1990 to 2013. Golden married Simone De Staley in 2015. They live in [[Hendersonville, Tennessee]].{{citation needed|date=August 2016}} He has four sons, Rusty, Craig, Chris and Solomon, a step-daughter and seven grandchildren. {{citation needed|date=August 2016}} Golden's sons Rusty and Chris recorded as [[The Goldens]] for [[Epic Records]] and [[Capitol Records]] between 1988 and 1991.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> They also played in his road band during his solo career.<ref name=\"news\"/>\n\n==The \"Golden Era Plantation\"==\n[[File:goldentree1.jpg|thumb|right|Golden's likeness is carved into the side of an oak tree on the edge of the property, which is visible from the road]]\n\nGolden's home is called The \"Golden Era Plantation.\" Built in 1786, it is recognized as the oldest brick home in [[Sumner County, Tennessee]]. The [[Federal architecture|Federal-style]] structure was built in 1786, then called \"Pilot's Knob,\" on a military outpost by [[American Revolutionary War]] Captain James Franklin, the father of planter and slave trader [[Isaac Franklin]] (1789\u20131846). After the war, he was awarded a land grant to the property.\n\nDuring the [[American Civil War|Civil War]], the Plantation became a station camp for [[Confederate States Army|Confederate]] soldiers. In order to protect their valuable gold and silver from approaching [[Union Army|Union]] soldiers, the occupants buried the metals in the ground surrounding the house. This gold was later discovered during renovation of the home in 1976.\n\nThe area has been struck twice by [[tornado]]es; once in 1892 and again on [[April 6\u20138, 2006 Tornado Outbreak|April 6, 2006]]. Originally a two-story building, the second story was removed by the first tornado. Repairs were made leaving it as a single-story home. Following the second tornado, the home's architecture was restored, adding a second story. William Lee Golden still resides at Golden Era. <ref>{{cite web |url=http://yoursumner.com/passing-on-the-torch-for-a-golden-era/ |title=Passing on the Torch for a Golden Era - YourSumner |website=yoursumner.com |access-date=13 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160311093132/http://yoursumner.com/passing-on-the-torch-for-a-golden-era/ |archive-date=11 March 2016 |url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n=== Albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! Carter|A.P.]] and [[Sara Carter]], was an American musician involved in the preservation of [[Appalachian music]].\n\nCarter was born on July 2, 1923, in [[Maces Spring, Virginia]].<ref name=\"McCloud\">{{cite book |last=McCloud |first=Barry |date=1995 |title=Definitive Country: The Ultimate Encyclopedia of Country Music and Its Performers |url=https://archive.org/details/definitivecountr00mccl/page/141/mode/1up?view=theater |url-access=registration |edition=First |location=New York |publisher=Berkley Publishing Group |pages=141\u2013142 |isbn=9780399518904 |oclc=30735303}}</ref> She and her brother [[Joseph Dougherty Carter|Joe]] performed with their parents on a series of recordings for the Acme label.<ref>{{cite book | url=https://books.google.com/books?id=AY7St4-8x10C&dq=Janette+Carter&pg=PA529 | isbn=9780252068812 | title=Long Steel Rail: The Railroad in American Folksong | year=2000 | publisher=University of Illinois Press }}</ref> Janette and Joe later recorded material together consisting of works they had written and songs previously recorded by members of the Carter family.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://books.google.com/books?id=PPzZAAAAMAAJ&q=%22Joe+and+Janette+Carter%22+1966 | title=Folk Review | year=1976 | publisher=Folk review }}</ref>\n\nIn 1976, Carter and community members built an 880-seat amphitheater, the [[Carter Family Fold]], beside the [[A. P. Carter Store]] which her father had operated after the [[Carter Family]] had disbanded as a musical group. The Carter Family Fold attracts more than 50,000 visitors a year.<ref name=\"nhf\">{{cite web|url=https://www.arts.gov/honors/heritage/janette-carter |title=Janette Carter: Country musician, advocate |author=<!--Not stated--> |date=n.d. |website=www.arts.gov |publisher=National Endowment for the Arts |access-date=January 5, 2021}}</ref> Carter performed there weekly, until shortly before she died.<ref>{{cite magazine |author=<!--Staff writer(s); no by-line.--> |title=Notebook |magazine=Time |volume=167 |issue=6 |page=19 |date=February 6, 2006}}</ref>\n\nCarter had three children with her first husband, James Jett: Donald William, Rita Janette, and James Delaney (Dale).<ref>{{cite news |author=<!--not stated--> |date=January 26, 2007 |title=James Jett |url=https://www.legacy.com/obituaries/tricities/obituary.aspx?n=james-jett&pid=86144808 |work=Bristol Herald Courier |location=Bristol, Virginia |access-date=June 5, 2022}}</ref> She died on January 22, 2006, in [[Kingsport, Tennessee]], after battling [[Parkinson's disease]] and other illnesses.<ref name=\"NYT\">{{cite news |author=<!--not stated--> |date=January 24, 2006 |title=Janette Carter, 82, Carter Family musician |newspaper=The New York Times |page=B8 |edition=Late}}</ref> She was buried next to her mother, Sara Carter Bayes, and her brother, Joe, at the [[Mount Vernon United Methodist Church]] Cemetery in Maces Spring.\n[[File:Grave of Sara Carter Bayes and children at Mount Vernon United Methodist Church at Maces Springs, Virginia now Hiltons, Virginia.jpg|thumb|right|Grave of Janette Carter between her mother and brother, Joe]]\n\nCarter is a recipient of a 2005 [[National Heritage Fellowship]] awarded by the [[National Endowment for the Arts]], which is the United States' highest honor in the folk and traditional arts,<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.arts.gov/honors/heritage/year/2005 |title=NEA National Heritage Fellowships 2005 |author=<!--Not stated-->  |website=www.arts.gov |publisher=National Endowment for the Arts |access-date=January 5, 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200521114828/https://www.arts.gov/honors/heritage/year/2005 |archive-date=May 21, 2020 |url-status=dead}}</ref> in recognition for her lifelong advocacy for the performance and preservation of Appalachian music.<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.arts.gov/about/nearts/story.php?id=p07_carter&issue=2006_v1 |title=In Memoriam: Janette Carter (1923\u20132006) |publisher=National Endowment for the Arts |access-date=February 2, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120925194611/http://www.arts.gov/about/NEARTS/story.php?id=p07_carter&issue=2006_v1 |archive-date=September 25, 2012 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n==References==\n{{reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n*[http://www.carterfamilyfold.org/ Official Carter Family Fold Website]\n{{Carter
